\NormalFont\ShortTitle{Jeremiah}
{\MT Jeremiah

\par }\ChapOne{1}{\SH The Superscription
\par }{\PP \VerseOne{1}The following
is a record of what
Jeremiah
son
of Hilkiah
prophesied.
He was one of the priests
who
lived at Anathoth
in the territory
of the tribe of Benjamin.
\VS{2}The
{\ND{Lord}}
began
to speak
to
him in the thirteenth
year
that Josiah
son
of Amon
ruled over
Judah.
\VS{3}The
{\ND{Lord}} also spoke to him when
Jehoiakim
son
of Josiah
ruled over
Judah,
and he continued to speak to him until
the fifth
month
of the eleventh
year
that Zedekiah
son
of Josiah
ruled over
Judah.
That was when the people of Jerusalem
were taken into exile.
\par }{\SH Jeremiah’s Call and Commission
\par }{\PP \VS{4}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to me,
\par }{\Q \VS{5}“Before
I formed
you in your mother’s womb
I chose
you.

\par }{\Q Before
you were born
I set you apart.
\par }{\Q I appointed you to be a prophet
to the nations.”
\par }{\PP \VS{6}I answered,
“Oh,
Lord

{\ND{God}}, I really
do not
know
how to speak
well enough for
that, for I am
too young.”
\VS{7}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to
me, “Do not
say,
‘I am
too young.’
But
go
to whomever
I send
you and say whatever
I
tell you.
\VS{8}Do not
be afraid
of those to whom I send you, for
I
will be with
you to protect
you,” says
the
{\ND{Lord}}.
\VS{9}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}
reached
out his hand
and touched
my mouth
and said
to me,
“I
will most assuredly
give
you the words
you are to speak for me.
\VS{10}Know for
certain that I hereby
give you the authority to announce to nations
and kingdoms
that they will be uprooted
and torn
down, destroyed
and demolished,
rebuilt
and firmly planted.”
\par }{\SH Visions Confirming Jeremiah’s Call and Commission
\par }{\PP \VS{11}Later
the {\ND{Lord}}
asked
me, “What
do you
see,
Jeremiah?” I answered,
“I
see
a branch
of an almond tree.”
\VS{12}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}
said,
“You have observed
correctly.
This means
I am
watching
to make
sure my threats
are carried out.”
\par }{\PP \VS{13}The
{\ND{Lord}}
again
asked
me, “What
do you
see?” I answered,
“I
see
a pot
of boiling
water; it is tipped toward
us from the north.”
\VS{14}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}
said,
“This means
destruction
will break out from the north
on
all
who live
in the land.
\VS{15}For
I will soon
summon
all
the peoples
of the kingdoms
of the north,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}. “They will come
and their kings will set
up their thrones
near the entrances
of the gates
of Jerusalem.
They will attack
all
the walls
surrounding
it, and all
the towns
in Judah.
\VS{16}In this way
I will pass sentence
on
the people of Jerusalem and Judah because
of all
their wickedness.
For they rejected
me and offered
sacrifices to other
gods,
worshiping
what they made
with their own hands.”
\par }{\PP \VS{17}“But you,
Jeremiah, get
yourself ready! Go
and tell
these people everything
I
instruct
you to
say. Do not
be terrified
of them, or
I will give you good reason to be terrified of them.
\VS{18}I,
the
{\ND{Lord}}, hereby
promise to make
you as strong as a fortified
city,
an iron
pillar,
and a bronze
wall.
You will be able to stand up against
all
who live in the land,
including the kings
of Judah,
its officials,
its priests
and all the people
of the land.
\VS{19}They will attack
you but they will not
be able
to overcome you, for
I
will be with
you to rescue
you,” says
the {\ND{Lord}}.

\par }\Chap{2}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to
me. He said:
\VS{2}“Go
and declare
in the hearing
of the people of Jerusalem: ‘This is what
the
{\ND{Lord}}
says: “I have fond memories
of you, how devoted
you were to me in your early
years. I remember
how you loved
me like a new bride;
you followed
me
through the
wilderness,
through a land
that had
never
been planted.
\VS{3}Israel
was set apart
to the
{\ND{Lord}}; they were like the first fruits
of a harvest
to him. All
who tried to devour
them were punished;
disaster
came
upon them,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}.’ ”
\par }{\SH The Lord Reminds Them of the Unfaithfulness of Their Ancestors
\par }{\Q \VS{4}Now listen
to what
the Lord
has to say, you descendants of Jacob,
\par }{\Q all
you family
groups from the nation
of Israel.
\par }{\Q \VS{5}This is what
the Lord
says:
\par }{\Q “What
fault
could your ancestors
have possibly
found in me
\par }{\Q that
they strayed so far
from me?

\par }{\Q They paid allegiance
to worthless idols,
and so became worthless to me.
\par }{\Q \VS{6}They did not
ask:
\par }{\Q ‘Where
is the
{\ND{Lord}}
who delivered
us out of Egypt,
\par }{\Q who brought us through
the wilderness,
\par }{\Q through a land
of desert
sands and rift
valleys,
\par }{\Q through a land
of drought
and deep darkness,
\par }{\Q through a land
in which no
one
travels,
\par }{\Q and where
no
one
lives?’
\par }{\Q \VS{7}I brought
you into
a fertile
land
\par }{\Q so you could enjoy
its fruits
and its rich bounty.
\par }{\Q But when you entered
my land, you defiled
it;

\par }{\Q you made
the land
I call my own
loathsome to me.
\par }{\Q \VS{8}Your priests
did not
ask,
‘Where
is the
{\ND{Lord}}?’

\par }{\Q Those responsible
for teaching my law
did not
really know
me.

\par }{\Q Your rulers
rebelled against
me.
\par }{\Q Your prophets
prophesied
in the name of the god Baal.
\par }{\Q They all worshiped
idols that could not
help them.
\par }{\SH The Lord Charges Contemporary Israel with Spiritual Adultery
\par }{\Q \VS{9}“So,
once more
I will state
my case
against you,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q “I will also state
it against your children
and grandchildren.
\par }{\Q \VS{10}Go
west across
the sea to the coasts
of Cyprus
and see.
\par }{\Q Send
someone east to Kedar
and have them look carefully.
\par }{\Q See
if
such a thing as this has ever happened:
\par }{\Q \VS{11}Has a nation
ever changed
its gods
\par }{\Q (even though they
are not
really gods
at all)?
\par }{\Q But my people
have exchanged
me, their glorious
God,

\par }{\Q for a god
that cannot help them at all!
\par }{\Q \VS{12}Be amazed
at this,
O heavens!

\par }{\Q Be shocked
and utterly
dumbfounded,”
\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{13}“Do
so because
my people
have committed
a double
wrong:

\par }{\Q they have rejected
me,
\par }{\Q the fountain
of life-giving
water,
\par }{\Q and they have dug
cisterns
for themselves,
\par }{\Q cracked
cisterns
which
cannot
even hold
water.”
\par }{\SH Israel’s Reliance on Foreign Alliances (not on God)
\par }{\Q \VS{14}“Israel
is not a slave,
is he?
\par }{\Q He was not born
into slavery, was he?

\par }{\Q If not, why
then is he being
carried off?
\par }{\Q \VS{15}Like lions
his enemies roar
victoriously over
him;
\par }{\Q they raise
their voices
in triumph.

\par }{\Q They have laid his land
waste;
\par }{\Q his cities
have been burned
down and deserted.
\par }{\Q \VS{16}Even
the soldiers from Memphis
and Tahpanhes
\par }{\Q have cracked
your skulls, people of Israel.
\par }{\Q \VS{17}You have
brought all this
on yourself, Israel,

\par }{\Q by deserting
the {\ND{Lord}}
your God
when
he was leading
you along
the right path.
\par }{\Q \VS{18}What
good will it do you then to go down to
Egypt
\par }{\Q to seek help
from the Egyptians?

\par }{\Q What
good will it do you to go over
to Assyria
\par }{\Q to seek help
from the Assyrians?
\par }{\Q \VS{19}Your own wickedness
will bring about
your punishment.
\par }{\Q Your unfaithful acts
will bring down discipline
on you.

\par }{\Q Know,
then, and realize
how
utterly harmful
\par }{\Q it was for you to reject
me, the

{\ND{Lord}}
your God,
\par }{\Q to show
no
respect
for
me,”

\par }{\Q says
the Lord

{\ND{God}}
who rules over all.
\par }{\SH The Lord Expresses His Exasperation at Judah’s Persistent Idolat
\par }{\Q \VS{20}“Indeed,
long ago
you threw off
my authority
\par }{\Q and refused
to be subject to me.

\par }{\Q You said,
‘I will not
serve
you.’
\par }{\Q Instead,
you
gave yourself to other gods on
every
high
hill
\par }{\Q and under
every
green
tree,
\par }{\Q like a prostitute
sprawls out before her lovers.
\par }{\Q \VS{21}I
planted
you in the land
\par }{\Q like a special vine
of the very best stock.
\par }{\Q Why in the world have you turned
into something like a wild vine
\par }{\Q that produces rotten,
foul-smelling grapes?
\par }{\Q \VS{22}You can try to wash
away your guilt with a strong detergent.
\par }{\Q You can use as much
soap
as you want.
\par }{\Q But the stain
of your guilt
is still there for me to see,”

\par }{\Q says
the Lord

{\ND{God}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{23}“How
can you say,
‘I have not
made myself unclean.
\par }{\Q I have not
paid allegiance
to the gods called Baal.’
\par }{\Q Just look
at the way
you
have behaved in the Valley
of Hinnom!

\par }{\Q Think about the things you have
done
there!
\par }{\Q You are like a flighty,
young female camel
\par }{\Q that rushes here and there, crisscrossing
its path.
\par }{\Q \VS{24}You are like a wild female donkey
brought up
in the wilderness.
\par }{\Q In her lust
she sniffs
the wind
to get the scent of a male.

\par }{\Q No
one can
hold her back
when she is
in heat.
\par }{\Q None
of the males need wear themselves out chasing after her.
\par }{\Q At mating time
she is easy
to find.
\par }{\Q \VS{25}Do not chase after
other gods until your shoes wear out
\par }{\Q and your throats
become dry.
\par }{\Q But you say,
‘It is useless
for you to try and stop
me
\par }{\Q because
I love
those foreign
gods and want to pursue them!’
\par }{\Q \VS{26}Just as a thief
has to suffer dishonor
when
he is caught,
\par }{\Q so
the people
of Israel
will suffer
dishonor
for
what they
have done.

\par }{\Q So will their kings
and officials,
\par }{\Q their priests
and their prophets.
\par }{\Q \VS{27}They say
to a wooden
idol, ‘You
are my father.’
\par }{\Q They say to a stone
image, ‘You
gave birth
to me.’

\par }{\Q Yes,
they have
turned
away from me instead of turning
to me.

\par }{\Q Yet when they are in trouble,
they say,
‘Come and save us!’
\par }{\Q \VS{28}But where
are the gods
you made
for yourselves?
\par }{\Q Let them save
you when
you are in trouble.
\par }{\Q The sad fact is that
you have as many
gods
\par }{\Q as you have towns,
Judah.
\par }{\Q \VS{29}“Why
do you try to refute
me?

\par }{\Q All
of you have rebelled
against me,”
\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{30}“It did no good
for me to punish
your people.
\par }{\Q They did not
respond
to such correction.
\par }{\Q You slaughtered
your prophets
\par }{\Q like a voracious
lion.”
\par }{\Q \VS{31}You
people
of this generation,
\par }{\Q listen to what
the {\ND{Lord}}
says.
\par }{\Q “Have I been like a wilderness
to you, Israel?
\par }{\Q Have I been like a dark
and dangerous land
to you?

\par }{\Q Why
then do you say,
‘We are free to wander.
\par }{\Q We will not
come
to you any more?’
\par }{\Q \VS{32}Does a young woman
forget
to put on her jewels?
\par }{\Q Does a bride
forget to put on her bridal attire?
\par }{\Q But my people
have forgotten
me
\par }{\Q for more days
than can even be counted.
\par }{\Q \VS{33}“My, how
good
you have become
\par }{\Q at chasing
after your lovers!

\par }{\Q Why,
you could even
teach
prostitutes
a thing
or two!
\par }{\Q \VS{34}Even
your clothes
are stained
with
\par }{\Q the lifeblood
of the poor
who had not done anything wrong;
\par }{\Q you did not catch
them breaking
into your homes.

\par }{\Q Yet,
in spite of all
these things you have done,
\par }{\Q \VS{35}you say,
‘I have not done anything wrong,
\par }{\Q so the
{\ND{Lord}}
cannot really be angry
with me any
more.’
\par }{\Q But, watch out! I
will bring down judgment
on
you
\par }{\Q because
you say,
‘I have not
committed any sin.’
\par }{\Q \VS{36}Why
do you constantly
go
about
\par }{\Q changing
your political allegiances?

\par }{\Q You will get no help
from Egypt
\par }{\Q just as
you got no help
from Assyria.
\par }{\Q \VS{37}Moreover,
you will come
away from Egypt
\par }{\Q with your hands
covering your faces
in sorrow and shame

\par }{\Q because
the {\ND{Lord}}
will not allow your reliance
on
them to be successful
\par }{\Q and you will not gain any help from them.

\par }\Chap{3}{\PP \par }{\Q \VerseOne{1}“If
a man
divorces
his wife
\par }{\Q and she leaves
him and becomes
another
man’s
wife,
\par }{\Q he may not
take her
back
again.
\par }{\Q Doing
that would utterly defile
the land.
\par }{\Q But you,
Israel,
have given yourself as a prostitute
to many
gods.

\par }{\Q So what makes you think
you can
return
to
me?”

\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{2}“Look
up
at
the hilltops
and consider
this.

\par }{\Q You have had sex with other gods
on
every one of them.

\par }{\Q You waited for
those gods like a thief lying in wait
in the desert.
\par }{\Q You defiled
the land
by your wicked
prostitution to other gods.
\par }{\Q \VS{3}That is why the rains
have
been withheld,
\par }{\Q and the spring rains
have not
come.
\par }{\Q Yet in spite of this you are obstinate
as a prostitute.
\par }{\Q You refuse
to be ashamed of what you have done.
\par }{\Q \VS{4}Even now
you say
to me, ‘You are my father!

\par }{\Q You
have been my faithful companion
ever since I was young.
\par }{\Q \VS{5}You will not always
be angry
with me, will you?
\par }{\Q You will
not be mad
at me forever,
will you?’

\par }{\Q That is what
you say,
\par }{\Q but you continually do
all the evil
that you can.”
\par }{\PP \VS{6}When
Josiah
was king
of Judah, the
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to
me, “Jeremiah, you have no doubt seen what
wayward
Israel
has
done.
You have seen how she went
up to
every
high
hill
and under
every
green
tree
to give herself like a prostitute
to other gods.
\VS{7}Yet even after
she had done
all
that, I thought
that she might come back
to me. But she did not.
Her sister,
unfaithful
Judah,
saw what she did.
\VS{8}She also saw
that
I gave
wayward
Israel
her divorce
papers
and sent
her away because
of her adulterous
worship of other gods. Even after her unfaithful
sister
Judah
had seen this, she still was not
afraid,
and she too
went
and gave herself like a prostitute to other gods.
\VS{9}Because she took her prostitution
so lightly,
she defiled
the land
through her adulterous
worship of gods made of wood
and stone.
\VS{10}In spite
of all
this,
Israel’s sister,
unfaithful
Judah,
has not
turned back
to me
with any
sincerity;
she has only
pretended
to do
so,” says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\VS{11}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to
me, “Under the circumstances, wayward
Israel
could even be considered
less guilty than unfaithful
Judah.
\par }{\SH The Lord Calls on Israel and Judah to Repent
\par }{\PP \VS{12}“Go
and shout
this message
to my people in the countries in the north.
Tell
them,
\par }{\Q ‘Come back
to me, wayward
Israel,’
says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q ‘I will not
continue to look
on you with displeasure.
\par }{\Q For
I am
merciful,’
says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q ‘I will not
be angry
with you forever.
\par }{\Q \VS{13}However,
you must confess
that
you have done wrong,

\par }{\Q and that
you have rebelled
against the
{\ND{Lord}}
your God.
\par }{\Q You must
confess
that you have given yourself
to foreign
gods under
every
green
tree,
\par }{\Q and have not
obeyed
my commands,’ says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\PP \VS{14}“Come back
to me, my wayward
sons,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}, “for
I am
your true
master. If you do, I will take
one
of you from each town
and two
of you from each family group,
and I will bring
you back to Zion.
\VS{15}I will give
you leaders
who will be faithful to me. They will lead you with knowledge and insight.
\VS{16}In those days,
your population
will greatly
increase
in the land.
At that time,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}, “people
will no
longer
talk about having
the ark
that contains the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
covenant
with us.
They will not
call it to mind,
remember
it, or
miss
it. No, that will not
be done
any more!
\VS{17}At that time
the city of Jerusalem
will be called
the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
throne.
All
nations
will gather
there in
Jerusalem
to honor
the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
name. They will no
longer
follow
the stubborn inclinations
of their own evil
hearts.
\VS{18}At that time
the nation
of Judah
and the nation
of Israel
will be reunited.
Together
they
will come back
from a land
in the north
to the land
that
I gave
to your ancestors as a permanent possession. ”
\par }{\Q \VS{19}“I
thought
to myself,

\par }{\Q ‘Oh
what a joy
it would
be for me to treat
you like a son!

\par }{\Q What a joy
it would
be for me to give
you a pleasant
land,
\par }{\Q the most
beautiful
piece
of property
there is in all the world!’

\par }{\Q I thought
you would
call
me, ‘Father’
\par }{\Q and would never
cease being
loyal to me.
\par }{\Q \VS{20}But,
you have been unfaithful
to me, nation
of Israel,
\par }{\Q like an unfaithful
wife
who has left her husband,”
\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{21}“A noise
is heard
on
the hilltops.
\par }{\Q It is the sound of the people
of Israel
crying
and pleading
to their gods.
\par }{\Q Indeed
they have followed sinful
ways;
\par }{\Q they have forgotten
to be true to the

{\ND{Lord}}
their God.
\par }{\Q \VS{22}Come back
to me, you wayward
people.
\par }{\Q I want to cure
your waywardness.
\par }{\Q Say, ‘Here
we are. We come
to you
\par }{\Q because
you
are the
{\ND{Lord}}
our God.
\par }{\Q \VS{23}We know
our noisy
worship of false gods
\par }{\Q on the hills
and mountains
did not help us.

\par }{\Q We know
that the
{\ND{Lord}}
our God
\par }{\Q is the only one who can deliver
Israel.
\par }{\Q \VS{24}From earliest times our worship of that shameful
god, Baal,
\par }{\Q has taken away
all that our ancestors
worked
for.
\par }{\Q It has taken away our flocks
and our herds,
\par }{\Q and even our sons
and daughters.
\par }{\Q \VS{25}Let us acknowledge
our shame.
\par }{\Q Let us bear the disgrace
that we
deserve.

\par }{\Q For
we have sinned
against the
{\ND{Lord}}
our God,
\par }{\Q both we
and our ancestors.
\par }{\Q From earliest
times to this very
day
\par }{\Q we have not
obeyed
the {\ND{Lord}}
our God.’

\par }\Chap{4}{\PP \par }{\Q \VerseOne{1}“If
you, Israel,
want to come back,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}},
\par }{\Q “if
you want to come back
to
me

\par }{\Q you must get
those disgusting idols
out of my sight
\par }{\Q and must no
longer go astray.
\par }{\Q \VS{2}You must be truthful,
honest
and upright
\par }{\Q when you take an oath
saying, ‘As surely as the
{\ND{Lord}}
lives!’

\par }{\Q If you do, the nations
will pray to be as blessed
by him as you are
\par }{\Q and will make him the object of their boasting.”
\par }{\Q \VS{3}Yes,
the {\ND{Lord}}
has this
to say
\par }{\Q to the people
of Judah
and Jerusalem:
\par }{\Q “Like a farmer breaking up
hard unplowed ground,
\par }{\Q you must break your rebellious will and make a new beginning;
\par }{\Q just as a farmer must clear away thorns
lest the seed
is wasted,
\par }{\Q you must get rid of the sin that is ruining your lives.
\par }{\Q \VS{4}Just as ritual circumcision
cuts away
the foreskin
\par }{\Q as an external symbol
of dedicated covenant commitment,
\par }{\Q you must genuinely dedicate yourselves to the
{\ND{Lord}}
\par }{\Q and get rid of everything
that hinders
your commitment to me,

\par }{\Q people of Judah
and inhabitants
of Jerusalem.
\par }{\Q If you do not,
my anger
will blaze up
like a flaming
fire
against you
\par }{\Q that no one
will be able to extinguish.
\par }{\Q That will happen because of the evil
you have done.”
\par }{\SH Warning of Coming Judgment
\par }{\PP \VS{5}The
{\ND{Lord}} said,
\par }{\Q “Announce
this in Judah
and proclaim
it in Jerusalem:

\par }{\Q ‘Sound
the trumpet
throughout the land!’
\par }{\Q Shout out
loudly,
\par }{\Q ‘Gather together! Let us flee
into
the fortified
cities!’
\par }{\Q \VS{6}Raise
a signal flag
that tells people to go to Zion.
\par }{\Q Run for safety! Do not
delay!
\par }{\Q For
I
am about to bring
disaster
out of the north.
\par }{\Q It will bring great
destruction.
\par }{\Q \VS{7}Like a lion
that has come up
from its lair
\par }{\Q the one who destroys
nations
has set
out
from his home
base.

\par }{\Q He is coming out to lay
your land
waste.
\par }{\Q Your cities
will become ruins
and lie uninhabited.
\par }{\Q \VS{8}So put
on
sackcloth!
\par }{\Q Mourn
and wail,
saying,
\par }{\Q ‘The fierce
anger
of the {\ND{Lord}}
\par }{\Q has not
turned
away from us!’ ”
\par }{\Q \VS{9}“When
this
happens,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}},
\par }{\Q “the king
and his officials
will lose
their courage.
\par }{\Q The priests
will be struck with horror,
\par }{\Q and the prophets
will be speechless in astonishment.”
\par }{\PP \VS{10}In response to all this I said,
“Ah,
Lord

{\ND{God}}, you have surely
allowed
the people
of Judah and Jerusalem
to be deceived by those who
say,
‘You will be safe!’ But in fact
a sword
is already at our throats.”
\par }{\Q \VS{11}“At that time

\par }{\Q ‘A scorching

\par }{\Q from the hilltops

\par }{\Q It will

\par }{\Q for winnowing

\par }{\Q \VS{12}No, a wind

\par }{\Q Yes, even

\par }{\Q \VS{13}Look! The enemy is approaching

\par }{\Q The roar of his chariots

\par }{\Q His horses

\par }{\Q I cry out, “We are doomed,
for

\par }{\Q \VS{14}“Oh people of Jerusalem,

\par }{\Q so that you may

\par }{\Q How long

\par }{\Q wicked schemes

\par }{\Q \VS{15}For

\par }{\Q from the city of Dan

\par }{\Q \VS{16}They are saying,

\par }{\Q “Those who besiege

\par }{\Q like men guarding

\par }{\Q because

\par }{\Q says

{\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{18}“The way

\par }{\Q will bring this

\par }{\Q This

\par }{\Q The pain will be so

\par }{\PP \VS{19}I said,

\par }{\Q “Oh, the feeling in the pit

\par }{\Q I writhe in anguish.
\par }{\Q Oh, the pain
in my heart!

\par }{\Q My heart
pounds
within me.
\par }{\Q I cannot

\par }{\Q For

\par }{\Q the sound of the battle

\par }{\Q \VS{20}I see one destruction
after another

\par }{\Q so that

lies in ruins.
\par }{\Q I see our tents
suddenly
destroyed,
\par }{\Q their curtains torn

\par }{\Q \VS{21}“How long
must I see
the enemy’s battle flags
\par }{\Q and hear
the military signals
of their bugles?”
\par }{\PP \VS{22}The
{\ND{Lord}} answered,

\par }{\Q “This will happen because
my people
are foolish.
\par }{\Q They do not

\par }{\Q They are like children
who have no sense.
\par }{\Q They have no
understanding.
\par }{\Q They
are skilled
at doing evil.
\par }{\Q They do not

\par }{\Q \VS{23}“I looked

\par }{\Q I looked up

and its light
had vanished.
\par }{\Q \VS{24}I looked
at the mountains
and saw
that they were shaking.
\par }{\Q All

were swaying
back and forth!
\par }{\Q \VS{25}I looked
and saw
that there
were no

\par }{\Q and that all

\par }{\Q \VS{26}I looked

had become a desert
\par }{\Q and that all
of the cities
had been laid
in ruins.
\par }{\Q The
{\ND{Lord}}
had brought this all about
\par }{\Q because

\par }{\Q \VS{27}All this
will happen because

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q “The whole

\par }{\Q however, I will not

\par }{\Q \VS{28}Because

\par }{\Q and the sky

\par }{\Q For

\par }{\Q and I will not

\par }{\Q the people of every

\par }{\Q Others will climb

\par }{\Q All

\par }{\Q No

\par }{\Q \VS{30}And you,

\par }{\Q you accomplish

\par }{\Q decking

in jewels

\par }{\Q and putting on

\par }{\Q You are making yourself beautiful

\par }{\Q Your lovers

\par }{\Q They want

\par }{\Q \VS{31}In fact, I hear

\par }{\Q a cry

\par }{\Q It is the cry of Daughter
Zion
gasping
for

\par }{\Q reaching out for

\par }{\Q My life
is ebbing away before these murderers!”

\par }\Chap{5}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}} said,

\par }{\Q “Go up and down through

\par }{\Q \VS{23}But these

\par }\Chap{6}{\PP \par }{\Q \VerseOne{1}“Run for safety,

\par }{\Q “All

\par }{\Q \VS{30}They are regarded

\par }\Chap{7}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to
Jeremiah:
\VS{2}“Stand

{\ND{Lord}}’s

\VS{3}The

{\ND{Lord}}

of Israel

you to continue

\VS{4}Stop

that says, “We are safe! The temple
of the {\ND{Lord}}

of the {\ND{Lord}}
is here! The temple
of the {\ND{Lord}} is here!”
\VS{5}You must

\VS{6}Stop

\VS{7}If you stop doing these things, I will allow

to your ancestors
as

\par }{\PP \VS{8}“‘But just look

\VS{9}You steal.

You commit adultery.

You pay allegiance

\VS{10}Then you come
and stand
in my presence
in this
temple
I have
claimed
as my own
and say,
“We are
safe!” You think you are
so
safe that you go
on
doing
all
those hateful sins!
\VS{11}Do you think this
temple
I have claimed
as
my own
is to be
a hideout
for robbers? You had better take note! I
have seen
for myself what you have done! says
the
{\ND{Lord}}.
\VS{12}So, go
to
the place
in Shiloh
where
I allowed
myself to be worshiped
in the early days.
See
what
I did
to it because
of the wicked
things my people
Israel did.
\VS{13}You also have
done
all
these
things,
says
the {\ND{Lord}}, and I have spoken
to
you over and over again.
But
you have not
listened! You have refused
to respond
when I called
you to repent!
\VS{14}So
I will destroy this temple
which
I have claimed
as my own,
this temple that
you
are trusting
to protect you. I will destroy this place
that
I gave
to you and your ancestors,
just
like I destroyed Shiloh.
\VS{15}And I will drive
you out
of my sight
just
like I drove
out your relatives,
the people
of Israel.’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{16}Then the
{\ND{Lord}} said, “As for you,
Jeremiah, do not
pray
for
these
people! Do not
cry out
to me or petition
me on their behalf! Do not
plead
with me to save them, because
I will not

\VS{17}Do

what
they
are doing
in the towns
of Judah
and in the streets
of Jerusalem?
\VS{18}Children
are gathering
firewood,
fathers
are building
fires
with it, and
women
are mixing
dough
to bake cakes
to offer
to the goddess they call the Queen
of Heaven.
They are
also pouring
out drink offerings
to other
gods.
They seem to do
all this
just
to trouble me.
\VS{19}But
I am not
really
the one being troubled!” says
the {\ND{Lord}}. “Rather
they are bringing trouble on themselves to their own shame!
\VS{20}So,”
the Lord

{\ND{God}}
says,
“my raging
fury
will be poured
out on
this
land.
It will be poured
out on
human
beings and animals,
on
trees
and crops.
And it will burn
like a fire which cannot
be extinguished.”
\par }{\PP \VS{21}The
{\ND{Lord}} said
to the people of Judah, “The
{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says: ‘You might as well go ahead and add
the meat
of your burnt offerings
to that of the other sacrifices
and eat it, too!
\VS{22}Consider this: When

after

\VS{23}I also

If

Live

\VS{24}But they did not

They acted
worse and worse
instead

\VS{25}From

the land
of Egypt

\VS{26}But your ancestors
did not

and were more wicked
than even their own forefathers.’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{27}Then the
{\ND{Lord}} said
to
me, “When you tell them
all

\VS{28}So tell

is a nation
that has not
obeyed
the {\ND{Lord}}
their God
and has not

Faithfulness

\VS{29}So, mourn, you people of this nation. Cut off
your hair

Sing

on
the hilltops.
For
the {\ND{Lord}}
has decided to reject

\par }{\PP \VS{30}The
{\ND{Lord}}
says,
“I have rejected them because
the people
of Judah
have done
what I consider evil.
They have set up
their disgusting idols
in the temple
which
I have claimed
for my own
and have defiled it.
\VS{31}They have
also built
places of worship
in a place called Topheth
in the Valley
of Ben Hinnom
so that
they can sacrifice
their sons
and daughters
by fire.
That
is something I never commanded
them to do! Indeed, it never
even entered
my mind to command such a thing!
\VS{32}So,
watch
out!” says
the {\ND{Lord}}. “The time
will soon come
when people will no
longer
call those places Topheth
or the Valley
of Ben Hinnom.
But
they will call that valley
the Valley of Slaughter
and they will bury
so many people in Topheth
they will run
out of room.
\VS{33}Then the dead bodies
of these
people
will be
left on the ground for the birds
and wild
animals
to eat.
There will not
be any
survivors to scare them away.
\VS{34}I will put an end
to the sounds
of joy
and gladness,
or the glad celebration
of brides
and grooms
throughout the towns
of Judah
and the streets
of Jerusalem.
For
the whole land
will become
a desolate wasteland.”

\par }\Chap{8}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
says,
“When
that time
comes,
the
bones
of the kings
of Judah
and its

the
bones
of the priests
and prophets

in Jerusalem

from their graves.
\VS{2}They will be spread out
and exposed to the sun,
the moon
and the stars.
These are things they adored
and served,
things to which
they paid
allegiance,
from which
they sought
guidance, and worshiped.
The bones of these people will never
be regathered
and reburied.
They will
be like manure
used to fertilize the ground.
\VS{3}However, I will leave
some of
these wicked
people
alive
and banish
them to other
places.
But wherever
these people who survive
may go,
they will wish
they had died
rather than lived,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
\par }{\SH Willful Disregard of God Will Lead to Destruction

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\SH Jeremiah Laments over the Coming Destruction

\par }\Chap{9}{\PP \par }{\Q \VerseOne{1}I

\par }{\SH The Lord Laments That He Has No Choice But to Judge Them

\par }{\SH The Coming Destruction Calls For Mourning

\par }{\Q And we will be able to bear it!’
\par }{\Q \VS{20}But our tents

\par }{\Q no one left

\par }{\Q and the people

\par }{\Q The rumble

\par }{\Q places where only

\par }{\Q It is not

\par }\Chap{11}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to

\VS{2}“Hear

on

\VS{3}Tell

{\ND{Lord}},

\VS{4}Those are the terms that

that place which was like an iron-smelting furnace.

and I

\VS{5}Then

{\ND{Lord}}!”
\par }{\PP \VS{6}The

\VS{8}But they did not

\par }{\PP \VS{9}The
{\ND{Lord}}

“The people

\VS{10}They have gone back

\VS{11}So

\VS{12}Then

\VS{13}This

have as many

\VS{14}So, Jeremiah, do not

Do not

I will not

to

\par }{\PP \VS{15}The

\par }{\Q “What

\par }{\Q Many

\par }{\SH A Plot Against Jeremiah is Revealed and He Complains of Injustice

\par }\Chap{12}{\PP \par }{\Q \VerseOne{1}{\ND{Lord}}, you

\par }\Chap{13}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The

\par }{\SH Judgment for Believing the Misleading Lies of the False Prophets
\par }{\PP \VS{11}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{12}Even if

\par }{\PP \VS{13}Then I said,
“Oh,

{\ND{God}}, look! The prophets

\par }{\PP \VS{14}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}
said

\VS{15}I

‘No

\VS{16}The people

and there will be no

This will happen to the men and their
wives,
their sons,
and their daughters.
For I will pour
out on

\par }{\SH Lament over Present Destruction and Threat of More to Come
\par }{\Q \VS{17}“Tell

\par }{\Q ‘My eyes

\par }{\Q day

\par }{\Q For

\par }{\Q They have suffered

\par }{\Q \VS{18}If

\par }{\Q I see

\par }{\Q If

\par }{\Q I see

\par }{\Q For

\par }{\Q in the land

\par }{\PP \VS{19}Then I
said,
\par }{\Q “{\ND{Lord}}, have you completely rejected
the nation of Judah?
\par }{\Q Do you despise the city
of Zion?
\par }{\Q Why

\par }{\Q that we are beyond recovery?

\par }{\Q We hope

\par }{\Q We hope for a time
of relief
from our troubles, but experience terror.
\par }{\Q \VS{20}{\ND{Lord}}, we confess
that we have been wicked.
\par }{\Q We confess
that our ancestors
have done wrong.

\par }{\Q We have indeed

\par }{\Q \VS{21}For

\par }{\Q Do not

\par }{\Q Be mindful

with

\par }{\Q \VS{22}Do any of the worthless idols

\par }{\Q Do the skies

\par }{\Q Is it not
you,
O Lord
our God,
who does this?

\par }{\Q So we put
our hopes
in you

\par }{\Q because
you
alone do
all

\par }\Chap{15}{\PP \VerseOne{1}Then the
{\ND{Lord}}
said to me,
“Even if

\VS{2}If

{\ND{Lord}}
says

\par }{\Q “Those who

\par }{\Q Those who are destined to die in war

\par }{\Q Those who

\par }{\Q Those who

\par }{\PP \VS{3}“I will punish

\par }{\PP \VS{5}The

\par }{\Q “Who

\par }{\Q I have grown tired

\par }{\Q I will do so because they did not

\par }{\Q \VS{9}The mother who had

\par }{\Q to be killed in war by the onslaughts

\par }{\PP says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\SH Jeremiah Complains about His Lot and The Lord Responds
\par }{\PP \VS{10}I said,

\par }{\Q “Oh,

\par }{\Q I am always starting arguments

\par }{\Q I have not

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q I will again allow you to be

\par }{\Q a fortified

\par }{\Q but they will not

\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{21}“I will deliver

of the wicked.
\par }{\Q I will free you

\par }\Chap{16}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to me,
\VS{2}“Do not

and do not

\VS{3}For

{\ND{Lord}}, tell

\VS{4}They will die

Their corpses

\par }{\PP \VS{5}“Moreover

{\ND{Lord}}, tell

{\ND{Lord}}, so affirm it!
\VS{6}Rich

\VS{7}No one

\par }{\SH The Lord Promises Exile (But Also Restoration)
\par }{\PP \VS{10}“When

{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{11}Then tell

\VS{12}And you

\VS{18}Before

\par }{\PP \VS{19}Then I said,

\par }{\Q “{\ND{Lord}}, you give me strength

\par }{\Q No, what

\par }{\PP \VS{21}The
{\ND{Lord}} said,

\par }{\Q “So

–
\par }{\Q I will let them know

\par }{\Q Then they will know

{\ND{Lord}}.”

\par }{\SH Individuals Are Challenged to Put Their Trust in the Lord

\par }{\SH Jeremiah Appeals to the Lord for Vindication

\par }{\SH Observance of the Sabbath Day Is a Key to the Future
\par }{\PP \VS{19}The

{\ND{Lord}}
told
me,
“Go
and stand
in the People’s
Gate
through which
the kings
of Judah
enter
and leave
the city. Then go and stand in all
the other gates
of the city of Jerusalem.
\VS{20}As you stand in those
places announce,
‘Listen,
all

pass
through these

Listen, all you kings
of Judah,
all

and all

of Jerusalem.
Listen

the {\ND{Lord}} says.
\VS{21}The
{\ND{Lord}}

‘Be very careful

\VS{22}Do not

{\ND{Lord}}, as I commanded

\VS{23}Your ancestors,

\VS{24}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{25}If you do this,

\VS{26}Then people will come

in Judah,

from the territory
of Benjamin,
from

from

and from
the southern

of the {\ND{Lord}}: burnt offerings,

and incense

\VS{27}But you
must
obey
me and set
the
Sabbath
day
apart
to me. You must not
carry
any loads
in through the gates
of Jerusalem
on the Sabbath
day.
If you disobey, I will set
the gates
of Jerusalem on fire.
It will burn down
all the fortified dwellings
in Jerusalem
and no one
will be able to put it out.’ ”

\par }\Chap{18}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to
Jeremiah:
\VS{2}“Go
down
at once to the potter’s
house.
I will speak to you further
there.”
\VS{3}So I went down
to the potter’s
house
and found
him working
at his wheel.
\VS{4}Now and then there would be something wrong
with the pot
he was
molding
from the clay
with his hands.
So he would rework
the clay
into another
kind of pot
as
he saw fit.
\par }{\PP \VS{5}Then
the {\ND{Lord}}
said
to me,
\VS{6}“I,
the {\ND{Lord}}, say: ‘O nation
of Israel,

I
not
deal

deals

you,

\VS{7}There are times,

\VS{8}But if that

I threatened
stops doing wrong,
I will cancel

I intended

\VS{9}And there are times
when

to build

\VS{10}But

displeases
me and does not

me,

\VS{11}So now,

of Judah

{\ND{Lord}}

‘I am

you have been living and do what is right.’
\VS{12}But they just keep saying,
‘We do not care what you say! We will do
whatever we want to do! We will continue
to behave wickedly
and stubbornly!’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{13}Therefore,
the {\ND{Lord}}
says,
\par }{\Q “Ask

\par }{\Q whether they have heard

\par }{\Q Israel

\par }{\Q But she has done

\par }{\Q Do

\par }{\Q \VS{15}Yet

\par }{\Q and offered sacrifices

\par }{\Q This makes them stumble

\par }{\Q and leave the old reliable

\par }{\Q They have left them to walk

\par }{\Q in roads

\par }{\Q \VS{16}So their land

\par }{\Q People will forever

\par }{\Q All

\par }{\Q and will shake

\par }{\Q \VS{17}I will scatter

\par }{\Q like dust blowing
in front

\par }{\Q I will turn my back on them and not
look
favorably on them

\par }{\Q when
disaster strikes them.”
\par }{\SH Jeremiah Petitions the Lord to Punish Those Who Attack Him
\par }{\PP \VS{18}Then some people said,
“Come

how to deal

to instruct us, wise men
to give us advice,
and prophets
to declare God’s word.
Come on! Let’s bring charges against him and get rid of
him! Then we will not
need to pay attention
to
anything
he says.”
\par }{\PP \VS{19}Then I said,

\par }{\Q “{\ND{Lord}}, pay attention
to
me.
\par }{\Q Listen
to what my enemies
are saying.
\par }{\Q \VS{20}Should
good
be paid
back with evil?
\par }{\Q Yet

to kill

\par }{\Q Just remember

before
you
\par }{\Q pleading

\par }{\Q to keep you from venting

\par }{\Q \VS{21}So

\par }{\Q Let them be cut down

\par }{\Q Let

\par }{\Q Let the older men

\par }{\Q and the younger men

\par }{\Q \VS{22}Let cries

\par }{\Q Do not
pardon their crimes!
\par }{\Q Do
not
ignore their sins
as though you had erased
them!

\par }{\Q Let
them be
brought down in defeat
before
you!
\par }{\Q Deal
with them while you are still angry!

\par }\Chap{19}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
told
Jeremiah, “Go
and buy
a clay jar
from a potter.
Take with you some of the leaders
of the people
and some of the leaders
of the priests.
\VS{2}Go out
to
the part of the Hinnom
Valley
which
is near the entrance
of the Potsherd
Gate.
Announce
there
what
I tell you.
\VS{3}Say,
‘Listen
to what
the {\ND{Lord}}
says, you kings
of Judah
and citizens
of Jerusalem! The
{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says, “I
will bring
a disaster
on
this
place
that
will make the ears
of everyone
who hears
about it ring!
\VS{4}I will do so because
these people have rejected
me and have defiled
this
place.
They have offered
sacrifices in it to other
gods
which
neither they
nor their ancestors
nor the kings
of Judah
knew anything about. They have filled
it with the
blood
of innocent children.
\VS{5}They have built
places
here for worship
of the god Baal
so that they could sacrifice
their children
as burnt offerings
to him in the fire.
Such sacrifices are something I never
commanded
them to make! They are something I never
told
them to do! Indeed, such a thing never
even entered
my mind!
\VS{6}So
I,
the {\ND{Lord}}, say: “The time
will soon come
that people will no
longer
call
this
place
Topheth
or the Hinnom
Valley.
But
they will call this valley the Valley
of Slaughter!
\VS{7}In this
place
I will thwart
the plans
of the people of Judah
and Jerusalem.
I will deliver them over to the power of their enemies
who are seeking
to kill them. They will die by the sword
at the hands
of their enemies. I will make
their dead bodies
food
for the birds
and wild beasts to eat.
\VS{8}I will make
this
city
an object of horror,
a thing to be hissed
at. All
who pass by
it will be filled with horror
and will hiss out their scorn
because
of all
the disasters that have happened to it.
\VS{9}I will reduce
the people of this city to desperate
straits
during the siege
imposed on it by their enemies
who are seeking
to kill
them. I will make them so desperate that they will eat
the flesh
of their own sons
and daughters
and the flesh
of one
another.” ’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{10}The
{\ND{Lord}} continued, “Now break
the jar
in front
of those who
have come
here with you.
\VS{11}Tell
them
the

{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all
says, ‘I will do just
as Jeremiah has done.
I will smash
this
nation
and this
city
as
though it were
a potter’s
vessel
which
is broken
beyond repair.
The dead will
be buried
here in Topheth
until there is no
more room
to bury them.’
\VS{12}I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, say: ‘That is how I will deal with this
city
and its citizens.
I will make
it like Topheth.
\VS{13}The houses
in Jerusalem
and the houses
of the kings
of Judah
will be defiled
by dead bodies just like this place,
Topheth.
For they offered sacrifice
to the stars
and poured out
drink offerings
to other
gods
on
the roofs
of those
houses.’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{14}Then Jeremiah
left
Topheth
where
the {\ND{Lord}}
had sent
him to give that prophecy.
He went to the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple
and stood
in its courtyard
and called out
to
all
the people.
\VS{15}“The

{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says, ‘I will soon
bring
on
this
city
and all
the towns
surrounding it all
the disaster
I threatened
to do to it. I will do so because
they have stubbornly
refused to pay
any attention
to what
I have said!’ ”

\par }\Chap{20}{\PP \VerseOne{1}Now Pashhur
son
of Immer
heard
Jeremiah
prophesy
these
things.
He was
the priest
who was
chief of security in the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple.
\VS{2}When he
heard Jeremiah’s
prophecy, he had the prophet
flogged.
Then he put
him in
the stocks
which
were at the Upper
Gate
of Benjamin
in the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple.
\VS{3}But the next day
Pashhur
released
Jeremiah
from
the stocks.
When he did, Jeremiah
said
to him,
“The
{\ND{Lord}}’s
name
for
you is not
‘Pashhur’
but
‘Terror is Everywhere.’
\VS{4}For
the {\ND{Lord}}
says,
‘I
will make

terrified

all
of them die
by the swords
of their enemies.
I will
hand all
the people of Judah
over
to the king
of Babylon.
He will carry some of them away into exile
in Babylon
and he will kill
others of them with the sword.
\VS{5}I will hand over
all
the wealth
of this
city
to their enemies. I will hand over to them all
the fruits of the labor
of the people of this city and all
their prized possessions,
as well as all
the treasures
of the kings
of Judah.
Their enemies
will seize

and carry

\VS{6}You,
Pashhur,
and all

will go
into exile
in Babylon.
You will die
there
and you
will be buried
there.
The same thing will happen to all
your friends
to whom
you have prophesied
lies.’ ”
\par }{\SH Jeremiah Complains about the Reaction to His Ministry
\par }{\Q \VS{7}{\ND{Lord}}, you coerced
me into being a prophet,
\par }{\Q and I allowed you to do it.
\par }{\Q You overcame
my resistance and prevailed
over me.

\par }{\Q Now I have become
a constant laughingstock.
\par }{\Q Everyone
ridicules me.
\par }{\Q \VS{8}For
whenever
I prophesy,
I must cry out,
\par }{\Q “Violence
and destruction
are coming!”

\par }{\Q This
message
from the
{\ND{Lord}}
has made
me
\par }{\Q an object of
continual insults
and derision.
\par }{\Q \VS{9}Sometimes I think,
“I will make no
mention
of his message.
\par }{\Q I will not
speak
as his messenger any more.”
\par }{\Q But then
his message becomes
like a fire
\par }{\Q locked up inside
of me, burning
in my heart
and soul.
\par }{\Q I grow weary
of trying
to hold it in;
\par }{\Q I cannot
contain it.
\par }{\Q \VS{10}I hear
many
whispering words of intrigue against
me.
\par }{\Q Those who would cause me terror
are everywhere!

\par }{\Q They are saying, “Come on, let’s publicly
denounce
him!”

\par }{\Q All
my so-called
friends
are just watching
for
\par }{\Q something that would lead to my downfall.
\par }{\Q They say, “Perhaps
he can be enticed
into slipping up,
\par }{\Q so we can prevail over
him and get
our revenge
on him.
\par }{\Q \VS{11}But the
{\ND{Lord}}
is with
me to help me like an awe-inspiring
warrior.
\par }{\Q Therefore
those who persecute
me will fail
and will not
prevail
over
me.
\par }{\Q They will be thoroughly
disgraced
because
they did not
succeed.
\par }{\Q Their disgrace
will never
be forgotten.
\par }{\Q \VS{12}O
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all,
you test
and prove the righteous.
\par }{\Q You see
into people’s hearts
and minds.
\par }{\Q Pay
them back
for what they
have done
\par }{\Q because
I trust you to vindicate
my cause.
\par }{\Q \VS{13}Sing
to the
{\ND{Lord}}! Praise
the {\ND{Lord}}!
\par }{\Q For
he rescues
the oppressed from the clutches
of evildoers.
\par }{\Q \VS{14}Cursed
be the day
I was born!
\par }{\Q May that day
not
be
blessed
when my mother
gave birth to me.
\par }{\Q \VS{15}Cursed
be the man
\par }{\Q who
made my father
very glad
\par }{\Q when he brought him the news
\par }{\Q that a baby
boy
had been
born to him!
\par }{\Q \VS{16}May that man
be like the cities
\par }{\Q that
the
{\ND{Lord}}
destroyed
without
showing
any mercy.
\par }{\Q May he hear
a cry of distress
in the morning
\par }{\Q and a battle cry
at noon.
\par }{\Q \VS{17}For he did not
kill
me before I came from the womb,
\par }{\Q making my pregnant
mother’s
womb
my grave
forever.
\par }{\Q \VS{18}Why
did I ever
come forth
from my mother’s womb?
\par }{\Q All
I experience
is trouble
and grief,
\par }{\Q and I spend
my days
in shame.

\par }\Chap{21}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to

when King
Zedekiah
sent
to him
Pashhur

\VS{2}“Please

{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{3}Jeremiah
answered

Zedekiah
\VS{4}that
the {\ND{Lord}},
the God
of Israel,
says, ‘The
forces
at your disposal

\VS{5}In anger,

\VS{6}I will kill
everything living
in Jerusalem,

\VS{7}Then

{\ND{Lord}}, promise
that I will hand

of Judah,

and any of the people

He will slaughter

He will
not

or

\par }{\PP \VS{8}“But tell the people
of Jerusalem that the

{\ND{Lord}}

in life;

\VS{9}Those who stay

will die
in battle

Those who leave
the city and surrender
to the Babylonians
who are besieging
it will live.
They will
escape
with their lives.
\VS{10}For
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, say that I am determined
not

city
but to bring disaster
on it. It will be handed
over to the king
of Babylon
and he will
destroy
it with fire.’ ”

\par }\Chap{22}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\SH Oracles Against the False Prophets

\par }{\Q doing something that was disgusting.
\par }{\Q They prophesied
in the name of the god Baal
\par }{\Q and led my people
Israel
astray.
\par }{\Q \VS{14}But I see
the prophets
of Jerusalem
\par }{\Q doing something

\par }{\Q They are unfaithful
to me
\par }{\Q and continually prophesy

\par }{\Q So they give encouragement
to people who are doing evil,
\par }{\Q with the result that they do not
stop their evildoing.
\par }{\Q I consider all

\par }{\Q and the citizens
of Jerusalem as bad as the people of Gomorrah.
\par }{\Q \VS{15}So
then I,
the {\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all,
\par }{\Q have something to say concerning

\par }{\Q ‘I will make

\par }{\Q and drink

\par }{\Q For

are the reason

\par }{\Q that ungodliness
has spread throughout

\par }{\Q \VS{16}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q “Do not

\par }{\Q those prophets

\par }{\Q They

\par }{\Q They are reporting

\par }{\Q not

\par }{\Q ‘Things will go

\par }{\Q They say

\par }{\Q ‘Nothing

\par }{\Q \VS{18}Yet

{\ND{Lord}}’s

\par }{\Q so they could see

\par }{\Q Which of them have ever

\par }{\Q \VS{19}But

\par }{\Q will come like a storm!

\par }{\Q Like a raging

down
\par }{\Q on

\par }{\Q \VS{20}The anger
of the {\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q until

\par }{\Q In days

\par }{\Q you people will come to understand

\par }{\Q \VS{21}I did not

\par }{\Q Yet they

\par }{\Q I did not

\par }{\Q Yet they

\par }{\Q \VS{22}But if

\par }{\Q they would have proclaimed
my message
to my people.
\par }{\Q They would have caused my people
to turn
from their wicked ways
\par }{\Q and stop doing the evil
things they are doing.
\par }{\Q \VS{23}Do you people think
that I
am
some local deity
\par }{\Q and not the transcendent
God?”
 the
{\ND{Lord}}
asks.
\par }{\Q \VS{24}“Do you really think anyone
can hide

\par }{\Q where I
cannot

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q “Do you not

\par }{\Q the {\ND{Lord}}
asks.
\par }{\PP \VS{25}The
{\ND{Lord}} says, “I have heard
what
those prophets
who are prophesying
lies
in my name
are saying.
They are saying, ‘I
have had a dream! I have had a dream!’
\VS{26}Those prophets
are just prophesying
lies.
They are prophesying
the delusions
of their own minds.
\VS{27}How
long will they go on plotting
to make my
people
forget
who I am through the dreams
they tell
one
another? That is just
as bad as what their ancestors
did when they forgot
who I am by worshiping
the god Baal.
\VS{28}Let the prophet
who has had
a dream
go ahead and tell
his dream.
Let the person who
has
received my message
report
that message
faithfully.
What
is like straw
cannot compare
to what is like grain! I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\VS{29}My message
is like a fire
that purges
dross! It is like a hammer
that breaks a rock
in pieces! I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, so affirm it!
\VS{30}So
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm
that I am opposed
to those prophets
who steal
messages
from one
another that they claim are from me.
\VS{31}I,
the {\ND{Lord}},
affirm
that I am opposed
to those prophets
who are using
their own tongues
to declare,
‘The
{\ND{Lord}} declares….’
\VS{32}I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm
that I am
opposed
to those prophets who
dream
up lies
and report
them. They are misleading my
people
with their reckless
lies.
I
did not send
them. I did not commission
them.
They are not
helping
these
people
at all. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!”
\par }{\PP \VS{33}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to me,
“Jeremiah,

or

{\ND{Lord}}?’ Tell them, ‘You are the burden,
and I

the

{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\VS{34}I will punish any prophet,
priest,

“The
{\ND{Lord}}’s
message is burdensome.”
I will punish
both that person
and his whole family.’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{35}So I, Jeremiah, tell
you, “Each
of you people should say to his friend
or

‘How
did the
{\ND{Lord}}
answer? Or what

{\ND{Lord}}
say?’
\VS{36}You must no longer

{\ND{Lord}}’s

is burdensome.
For

really pertains to what

You are misrepresenting
the

the living

the {\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
\VS{37}Each

‘What

{\ND{Lord}}

did the
{\ND{Lord}}
say?’
\VS{38}But

of the {\ND{Lord}}

the {\ND{Lord}}

word to
you that

“The
{\ND{Lord}}’s
message is burdensome.”
But you used the words
“The
{\ND{Lord}}’s
message
is burdensome” anyway.
\VS{39}So
I
will carry you far off and throw
you

city
I gave
to you and to your ancestors
out

\VS{40}I will bring
on

and lasting

will never

\par }\Chap{24}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
showed
me two
baskets
of figs
sitting
before
his temple.
This happened after
King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
deported
Jehoiakim’s
son,
King

of Judah.
He deported him and the
leaders
of Judah,
along with
the craftsmen
and metal workers,
and took
them to Babylon.
\VS{2}One
basket
had very
good-looking
figs
in it. They
looked like those that had ripened early.
The other
basket
had very
bad-looking
figs
in it, so bad
they could not
be eaten.
\VS{3}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to
me, “What
do you
see,
Jeremiah?” I answered,
“I see figs.
The good
ones
look very
good.
But the bad
ones look very
bad,
so bad
that they cannot
be eaten.”
\par }{\PP \VS{4}The
{\ND{Lord}}
said
to me,
\VS{5}“I,
the {\ND{Lord}},
the God
of Israel,
say: ‘The
exiles
whom
I sent away
from
here
to the land
of Babylon
are like
those
good
figs.
I consider
them to be good.
\VS{6}I will look
after their welfare
and will restore
them to this
land.
There I will build
them up and will not
tear
them down. I will plant
them firmly in the land and will not
uproot them.
\VS{7}I will give
them the desire
to acknowledge
that
I am
the {\ND{Lord}}. I
will be
their God
and they will be
my people.
For
they will wholeheartedly
return
to me.’
\par }{\PP \VS{8}“I,
the {\ND{Lord}}, also solemnly assert: ‘King
Zedekiah
of Judah,
his officials,
and the
people who remain
in Jerusalem
or who have gone to live
in Egypt
are like those bad figs. I consider them to be just
like those bad figs
that
are so bad
they cannot be eaten.
\VS{9}I will
bring such disaster
on them that all
the kingdoms
of the earth
will be horrified.
I will make them an object of reproach,
a proverbial example of disaster.
I
will make them an object of ridicule,
an example
to be used in curses. That
is how
they will be remembered wherever
I banish them.
\VS{10}I
will bring war,
starvation,
and disease
on them until
they are completely destroyed from the land
I gave
them
and their ancestors.’ ”

\par }\Chap{25}{\PP \VerseOne{1}In the fourth

{\ND{Lord}} spoke to Jeremiah

of Judah.
(That was the same as the first

was king

\VS{2}So

to all

of Judah

\VS{3}“For the last twenty-three

But you would not

\VS{4}Over and over again

\VS{5}He said

\VS{6}Do not

\VS{7}So,

{\ND{Lord}}

But you have made me angry

\par }{\PP \VS{8}“Therefore,
the

{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{9}So I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm

\VS{10}I will put an end

of people grinding meal.

\VS{11}This

\par }{\PP \VS{12}“‘But when

{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\VS{13}I will bring

\VS{14}For
many

of the king of Babylon and his nation too.

\par }{\SH Judah and the Nations Will Experience God’s Wrath
\par }{\PP \VS{15}So the

{\ND{Lord}},
the God
of Israel,

It is filled with the wine
of my wrath.
Take it and make the

to

\VS{16}When they have drunk

For I

\par }{\PP \VS{17}So I took
the
cup
from the
{\ND{Lord}}’s

I made all

\VS{18}I made Jerusalem

I did it so Judah, its kings, and its officials would become an object of horror

\VS{19}I made all

\par }{\PP \VS{27}Then the
{\ND{Lord}} said

{\ND{Lord}}

{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{29}For

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\PP \VS{30}“Then, Jeremiah, make the following prophecy

{\ND{Lord}}

{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q ‘Disaster

\par }\Chap{26}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to Jeremiah at the beginning
of the reign
of Josiah’s
son,
King
Jehoiakim
of Judah.
\VS{2}The

{\ND{Lord}}
said,
“Go stand
in the courtyard
of the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple.
Speak
out
to all
the people who are coming
from the towns
of Judah
to worship
in the
{\ND{Lord}}’s

Tell them
everything
I command
you to tell
them.
Do not
leave out a single
word!
\VS{3}Maybe
they will pay attention
and each
of them
will stop
living
the evil
way
they do. If they do that,
then I will forgo
destroying
them as I
had intended
to do
because

things they have been doing.
\VS{4}Tell
them
that the
{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{5}You must
pay attention

I
have sent

But you have not

\VS{6}If you

do to this

And I will make
this
city
an example

\par }{\PP \VS{7}The priests,
the prophets,
and all

these

{\ND{Lord}}’s

\VS{8}Jeremiah

to

\VS{9}How dare

{\ND{Lord}}’s

\par }{\PP \VS{10}However, some of the officials
of Judah
heard

{\ND{Lord}}’s

from the royal

They set up court

{\ND{Lord}}’s temple.
\VS{11}Then the priests

They said, “This

to die
because
he prophesied
against this

You have
heard

\par }{\PP \VS{12}Then Jeremiah
made his defense before
all
the officials
and all
the people. “The
{\ND{Lord}}
sent
me to prophesy
everything
you have
heard
me say
against this
temple
and against this
city.
\VS{13}But
correct
the way
you have been living
and do what is right. Obey
the {\ND{Lord}}
your God.
If you do, the
{\ND{Lord}}
will forgo
destroying
you as
he threatened he would.
\VS{14}As
to my case, I
am
in your power.
Do

\VS{15}But

note

of murdering
an innocent
man. For
the {\ND{Lord}}
has sent
me to speak
all
this
where you can hear it. That
is the truth!”
\par }{\PP \VS{16}Then the officials
and all
the people
rendered
their verdict to
the priests
and the prophets.
They said, “This
man
should not
be condemned
to die.
For
he has spoken
to
us under the authority
of the
{\ND{Lord}}
our God.”
\VS{17}Then
some
of the elders
of Judah stepped forward and spoke
to
all
the people
gathered
there. They said,
\VS{18}“Micah
from Moresheth
prophesied
during
the time
Hezekiah
was king
of Judah.
He told
all
the people
of Judah,
\par }{\Q ‘The

{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all

\par }{\Q “Zion
will become a plowed
field.
\par }{\Q Jerusalem
will become a pile of rubble.
\par }{\Q The temple
mount
will become
a mere wooded
ridge.” ’
\par }{\PP \VS{19}King
Hezekiah
and all
the people of Judah
did not put
him to death,

Hezekiah show reverence
for the
{\ND{Lord}}
and seek
the
{\ND{Lord}}’s

{\ND{Lord}}
forgo

are on
the verge of bringing
great
disaster
on

\par }{\PP \VS{20}Now
there was
another
man
who prophesied
as the
{\ND{Lord}}’s

this city
and this land
just

son
of Shemaiah
from Kiriath Jearim.
\VS{21}When the king
and all
his bodyguards
and officials

But Uriah
found out about
it and fled
to Egypt

\VS{22}However, King
Jehoiakim
sent
some men
to Egypt,

son
of Achbor,
\VS{23}and they brought

from there.
They took

Jehoiakim,

and had his body
thrown
into
the burial place
of the common people.
\par }{\PP \VS{24}However,
Ahikam
son
of Shaphan
used his influence
to keep Jeremiah
from being
handed
over and executed
by the people.


\par }\Chap{27}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to Jeremiah
early
in the reign
of Josiah’s
son,
King
Zedekiah of Judah.
\VS{2}The

{\ND{Lord}}
told
me, “Make
a yoke out of leather straps
and wooden crossbars
and put
it on
your neck.
\VS{3}Use it to send
messages to
the kings
of Edom,
Moab,
Ammon,
Tyre,
to
King
Zedekiah
of Judah.
\VS{4}Charge
them to
give their masters
a message
from me. Tell
them, ‘The
{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says
to
give your masters this message.
\VS{5}“I
made
the earth
and the people
and animals
on

and great

and I give

I see fit.
\VS{6}I
have
at this time placed
all

of yours

Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon.
I have even

\VS{7}All

him and his son
and grandson
until

for his own nation
to fall. Then
many

\VS{8}But suppose

to King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon.
Suppose it will

to him. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm

I will use the king
of Babylon
to punish it with war,

and disease

\VS{9}So
do not

to

or to

by

They

to the king
of Babylon.’
\VS{10}Do not listen to them,
because
their
prophecies
are lies.
Listening to them will only cause you to
be taken far
away from your native land.
I will drive
you out
of your country and you will die in exile.
\VS{11}Things will go better for the nation
that
submits
to the yoke
of servitude
to the king
of Babylon
and is subject
to him. I will leave
that nation in
its native land.
Its people can continue to farm
it and live
in it. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!” ’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{12}I told
King
Zedekiah
of Judah
the same thing.
I said, “Submit
to the yoke
of servitude to the king
of Babylon. Be subject
to him and his people.
Then you will continue
to live.
\VS{13}There is no reason why
you
and your people
should die
in war
or from starvation
or disease! That’s
what
the {\ND{Lord}}
says
will happen to
any nation
that
will not
be subject
to the
king
of Babylon.
\VS{14}Do not
listen
to
the prophets
who are telling
you that you do not
need to serve
the king
of Babylon.
For
they
are prophesying
lies to you.
\VS{15}For
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm
that I did not
send
them. They
are prophesying
lies
to you. If you listen to them, I will drive
you and the prophets
who are prophesying
lies out of the land and you
will all die in exile.”
\par }{\PP \VS{16}I also told
the priests
and all
the people,
“The
{\ND{Lord}}
says,
‘Do not
listen
to
what

They are prophesying
to you that the valuable

taken from the
{\ND{Lord}}’s

from Babylon
very

But
they
are prophesying
a lie to you.
\VS{17}Do not
listen
to them.
Be subject
to the king
of Babylon.
Then you will continue to live.
Why
should this
city
be made a pile of rubble?’ ”
\VS{18}I also told them, “If
they
are really prophets
and the
{\ND{Lord}}
is

to them, let

to the
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
Let them plead with him not
to let the valuable articles
that are still left
in the
{\ND{Lord}}’s

in the royal

and in Jerusalem
be taken away to Babylon.
\VS{19}For
the

{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all
has already spoken about the two bronze pillars,
the large bronze basin called ‘The Sea,’
and the movable

He has already spoken about the rest
of the valuable articles
that are left
in this

\VS{20}He has already spoken about these things that King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
did not
take away
when he carried
Jehoiakim’s
son

of Judah
and the nobles
of Judah

\VS{21}Indeed,
the

{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
has already spoken about the valuable articles
that are left
in the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple,
in the royal

of Judah,
and in Jerusalem.
\VS{22}He has said, ‘They will be

to Babylon.
They will remain there
until
it is time
for me to show consideration
for them again. Then I will bring
them back and restore
them to
this
place.’
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm this!”

\par }\Chap{28}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The following events occurred

\par }{\PP \VS{10}The prophet

\par }{\PP \VS{17}In the seventh

\par }\Chap{29}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The prophet

\par }{\PP \VS{15}“You say,

\par }\Chap{30}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\SH Israel and Judah Will Be Delivered after a Time of Deep Distress

\par }{\PP \VS{5}Yes,

\par }{\SH Israel Will Be Restored and Join Judah in Worship
\par }{\PP \VS{2}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q “The people

\par }{\Q will find

in the wilderness
\par }{\Q as they journey
to find rest for themselves.
\par }{\Q \VS{3}In a far-off
land the
{\ND{Lord}}
will manifest himself to them.
\par }{\Q He will say to them, ‘I have loved
you with an everlasting
love.
\par }{\Q That is why

to be faithful to you.
\par }{\Q \VS{4}I will rebuild

\par }{\Q so that you will once again be built up.
\par }{\Q Once again

\par }{\Q and join

\par }{\Q \VS{5}Once again

\par }{\Q on the hills

\par }{\Q Those who plant

\par }{\Q will once again enjoy their fruit.

\par }{\Q when

\par }{\Q “Come! Let us go

\par }{\Q to worship the
{\ND{Lord}}
our God!” ’ ”

\par }{\Q Deliver those of Israel

\par }{\Q Blind
and lame

\par }{\Q so will pregnant women

\par }{\Q A vast

\par }{\Q I will lead

\par }{\Q along smooth

\par }{\Q I will do this
because
I am Israel’s

\par }{\Q Ephraim
is my firstborn son.’ ”
\par }{\Q \VS{10}Hear

\par }{\Q \VS{14}I will provide

\par }{\Q My people

\par }{\PP \VS{15}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q “A sound

\par }{\Q a sound

\par }{\Q and refusing to be comforted,

\par }{\Q \VS{16}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\Q Your children will return

{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\par }{\Q \VS{17}Indeed, there is
hope

\par }{\Q Your children

\par }{\Q I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\par }{\Q \VS{18}I have indeed heard

\par }{\Q We are ashamed

\par }{\Q \VS{20}Indeed,

\par }{\Q I still

\par }{\Q I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!

\par }{\Q For

\par }{\Q something as unique as a woman

\par }{\SH Judah Will Be Restored
\par }{\PP \VS{23}The

{\ND{Lord}}

of Israel

\par }{\Q “I will restore

\par }{\Q When

\par }{\Q the place where righteousness

\par }{\Q \VS{24}The land of Judah

\par }{\Q \VS{26}Then they will say, ‘Under these conditions

\par }{\Q when I wake up

\par }{\SH Israel and Judah Will Be Repopulated
\par }{\PP \VS{27}“Indeed,
a time
is coming,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}, “when I will cause
people
and animals
to sprout
up in the lands of Israel
and Judah.
\VS{28}In the past I saw
to it that
they were uprooted
and torn down,
that they were destroyed
and demolished.
But now I will see

and firmly planted.
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!”
\par }{\SH The Lord Will Make a New Covenant with Israel and Judah
\par }{\PP \VS{29}“When that time
comes, people will no
longer
say,
‘The parents
have eaten
sour grapes,
but the children’s
teeth
have grown numb.’
\VS{30}Rather, each person
will die
for his own sins.
The teeth
of the person
who eats
the sour grapes
will themselves grow numb.
\par }{\PP \VS{31}“Indeed,
a time
is coming,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}}, “when I will make
a new
covenant
with
the people of
Israel
and Judah.
\VS{32}It will not
be like the old covenant
that
I made
with
their ancestors
when
I delivered
them from
Egypt.
For they
violated
that covenant,
even though I
was like a faithful husband
to them,” says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\VS{33}“But
I will make a new covenant
with
the whole nation
of Israel
after
I plant
them
back in the land,” says
the {\ND{Lord}}. “I will put
my law
within
them and write
it on
their hearts
and minds. I will be
their God
and they
will be
my people.
\par }{\PP \VS{34}“People
will no
longer
need
to teach
their neighbors
and relatives
to know
me. For
all
of them,
from the least
important
to the most important,
will know
me,” says
the {\ND{Lord}}. “For
I will forgive
their sin
and will no
longer
call to mind
the wrong they have done.”
\par }{\SH The Lord Guarantees Israel’s Continuance
\par }{\Q \VS{35}The
{\ND{Lord}}
has made a promise
to Israel.
\par }{\Q He promises
it as the one who fixed
the sun
to give light
by day
\par }{\Q and the moon
and stars
to give light
by night.
\par }{\Q He promises it as the one who stirs
up the sea
so that its waves
roll.
\par }{\Q He promises it as the one who is known as the
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
\par }{\Q \VS{36}The
{\ND{Lord}}
affirms, “The descendants
of Israel
will
not
\par }{\Q cease forever to be a nation in my sight.
\par }{\Q That could only happen if the fixed ordering of the heavenly lights
\par }{\Q were to cease to operate before me.”
\par }{\Q \VS{37}The
{\ND{Lord}}
says,
“I
will not reject
all
the descendants
of Israel
\par }{\Q because
of all
that
they have
done.
\par }{\Q That
could only happen if
the heavens
above
could be measured
\par }{\Q or the foundations
of the earth
below
could
all be explored,”
\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\SH Jerusalem Will Be Enlarged
\par }{\PP \VS{38}“Indeed
a time
is coming,” says
the {\ND{Lord}}, “when
the city of Jerusalem will be rebuilt
as my special city.
It will be built
from the Tower
of Hananel
westward to the Corner
Gate.
\VS{39}The boundary line
will extend beyond that, straight
west from there
to the Hill
of Gareb
and then turn southward
to Goah.
\VS{40}The whole
valley
where dead bodies
and sacrificial ashes
are thrown and all
the terraced fields
out to the Kidron
Valley
on the east
as
far north as
the Horse
Gate
will be included within this city that is sacred
to the
{\ND{Lord}}. The city will
never
again
be torn
down or
destroyed.” ‘span class=”footnote” id=”footnote-50” ’‘span class=”key” ’50‘a href=”\#note-50” class=”backref” ’31:22‘/a’‘span class=”text” ’
{\IT{sn}}:
{\IT{Heb}} “create.” This word is always used with God as the subject and refers to the production of something new or unique, like the creation of the world and the first man and woman (
Gen 1:1; 2:3; 1:27; 5:1) or the creation of a new heavens and a new earth in a new age (
Isa 65:17), or the bringing about of new and unique circumstances (
Num 16:30). Here reference is made contextually to the new exodus, that marvelous deliverance which will be so great that the old will pale in comparison (see the first note on v.
9).

\par }\Chap{32}{\PP \VerseOne{1}In the tenth
year
that
Zedekiah
was ruling over
Judah
the {\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to
Jeremiah.
That
was the same as the eighteenth
year
of Nebuchadnezzar.
\par }{\PP \VS{2}Now at that time,
the armies
of the king
of Babylon
were besieging
Jerusalem.
The prophet
Jeremiah
was
confined
in the courtyard
of the guardhouse
attached to the royal
palace
of Judah.
\VS{3}For King
Zedekiah
had confined
Jeremiah there after he had reproved him for prophesying as he did. He had asked
Jeremiah, “Why
do you
keep prophesying
these things? Why do you keep saying
that the

{\ND{Lord}}
says, ‘I
will hand
this
city
over
to the king
of Babylon? I will let him capture it.
\VS{4}King
Zedekiah
of Judah
will not
escape
from the Babylonians.
He will certainly
be handed
over
to the king
of Babylon.
He must
answer personally
to the king of Babylon and confront
him face
to face.
\VS{5}Zedekiah
will be
carried
off to Babylon
and will remain there
until
I have fully dealt
with him.
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm
it! Even if
you continue to fight
against the Babylonians,
you cannot
win.’ ”
\par }{\PP \VS{6}So now, Jeremiah
said,
“The
{\ND{Lord}}
told
me,
\VS{7}‘Hanamel,
the son
of your uncle
Shallum,
will come
to
you soon. He will say
to you, “Buy
my field
at Anathoth
because
you are entitled
as my closest relative
to buy it.” ’
\VS{8}Now it happened just as the
{\ND{Lord}}
had said! My cousin
Hanamel
came
to me
in the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
He said
to me,
‘Buy
my
field
which
is at Anathoth
in the territory
of the tribe of Benjamin.
Buy
it for
yourself since you are entitled
as my closest relative
to take possession
of it for yourself.’ When this happened, I recognized
that
the {\ND{Lord}}
had indeed
spoken to me.
\VS{9}So I bought
the field
at Anathoth
from my cousin
Hanamel.
I weighed out
seven ounces
of silver and gave it to him to pay for it.
\VS{10}I signed
the deed
of purchase,
sealed
it, and had some men serve as witnesses
to the purchase. I weighed
out the silver
for him on a scale.
\VS{11}There were two copies
of the deed
of purchase.
One was sealed
and contained
the order of transfer and the conditions
of purchase. The other was left unsealed.
\VS{12}I
took
both copies
of the deed
of purchase
and gave them to
Baruch
son
of Neriah,
the son
of Mahseiah.
I gave them to him in the presence
of my cousin
Hanamel,
the witnesses
who had signed
the deed
of purchase,
and all
the Judeans
who were housed in
the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
\VS{13}In the presence
of all these people I instructed
Baruch,
\VS{14}‘The

{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says, “Take
these
documents,
both the
sealed
copy of the deed of purchase
and the unsealed
copy. Put
them in a clay jar
so that they may
be preserved
for a long
time to come.” ’
\VS{15}For
the

{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says, “Houses,
fields,
and vineyards
will again
be bought
in this
land.” ’
\par }{\SH Jeremiah’s Prayer of Praise and Bewilderment
\par }{\PP \VS{16}“After
I
had given
the copies
of the deed
of purchase
to
Baruch
son
of Neriah,
I prayed
to
the {\ND{Lord}},
\VS{17}‘Oh,
Lord

{\ND{God}}, you
did indeed
make
heaven
and earth
by your mighty power
and great
strength.
Nothing
is too hard for you!
\VS{18}You show
unfailing love
to thousands.
But you also punish children
for the sins
of their parents.
You are the great
and powerful
God
who is known
as the
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
\VS{19}You plan
great
things and you do mighty
deeds.
You see
everything
people
do.
You
reward
each
of them
for the way
they live
and for the things they do.
\VS{20}You
did miracles
and amazing
deeds in the land
of Egypt
which have had
lasting
effect.
By
this
means you gained both in Israel
and among humankind
a renown
that lasts to this
day.
\VS{21}You used your mighty power
and your great
strength
to perform miracles
and amazing deeds
and to bring
great
terror
on the Egyptians. By this means you brought
your people
Israel
out
of the land
of Egypt.
\VS{22}You kept
the promise
that you swore on oath
to their ancestors.
You gave
them a land
flowing
with milk
and honey.
\VS{23}But when they came
in and took possession
of it, they did not
obey
you or
live
as
you had
instructed
them. They did
not
do
anything
that
you commanded them
to do. So
you brought all
this
disaster on them.
\VS{24}Even now
siege ramps
have been built up
around the city
in order to capture
it. War,
starvation,
and disease
are sure to make
the city
fall into
the hands
of the Babylonians
who are attacking
it.
{\ND{Lord}}, you threatened
that
this would happen.
Now
you can see that it is already taking place.
\VS{25}The city
is sure to fall into the hands
of the Babylonians.
Yet, in spite of this, you,
Lord

{\ND{God}}, have said
to me,
“Buy
that field
with silver
and have the transaction
legally witnessed.” ’ ”
\par }{\SH The Lord Answers Jeremiah’s Prayer
\par }{\PP \VS{26}The
{\ND{Lord}}
answered
Jeremiah.
\VS{27}“I am
the {\ND{Lord}}, the God
of all
humankind.
There is, indeed,
nothing too
difficult for me.
\VS{28}Therefore
I,
the {\ND{Lord}}, say: ‘I will indeed
hand
this
city
over
to King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
and the Babylonian
army. They will capture it.
\VS{29}The Babylonian soldiers
that are attacking
this
city
will break into
it and set
it on fire.
They will burn
it down
along with
the houses
where
people have made
me angry
by offering sacrifices
to the god Baal
and by pouring out
drink offerings
to other
gods
on their rooftops.
\VS{30}This will happen
because
the people of Israel
and Judah
have repeatedly
done
what displeases
me from their earliest
history until now and because
they have repeatedly
made me angry
by the things they have done.
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\VS{31}This will happen because
the people of this city
have aroused my anger
and my wrath
since
the time
they built
it until
now.
They have
made me so angry that
I am determined to remove
it from my sight.
\VS{32}I am determined to do so
because
the people of Israel
and Judah
have made
me angry
with all
their wickedness
– they,
their kings,
their officials,
their priests,
their prophets,
and especially
the people
of Judah
and the citizens
of Jerusalem
have done this wickedness.
\VS{33}They have turned
away from me
instead of turning
to
me.
I tried over
and over again
to instruct
them, but
they did not
listen
and respond to correction.
\VS{34}They set
up their disgusting idols
in the temple
which
I have claimed
for my own
and defiled it.
\VS{35}They built
places of worship
for the god Baal
in the Valley
of Ben
Hinnom
so that they could sacrifice
their sons
and daughters
to the god Molech.
Such
a disgusting practice was not
something I commanded
them to do! It never
even entered
my mind
to command them to do
such a thing! So
Judah
is certainly liable
for punishment.’
\par }{\PP \VS{36}“You
and your people
are right
in saying,
‘War,
starvation,
and disease
are sure to make
this city fall into the hands
of the king
of Babylon.’
But now
I,
the {\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel,
have something further to
say about this
city:
\VS{37}‘I
will certainly regather
my people from all
the countries
where
I will have exiled
them in my anger,
fury,
and great
wrath.
I will bring them back
to
this
place
and allow them to live
here in safety.
\VS{38}They will be
my people,
and I
will be
their God.
\VS{39}I will give
them a single-minded
purpose
to live in a way
that always
shows respect
for me. They will want to do that
for their own good and the good
of the children
who descend from them.
\VS{40}I will make
a lasting
covenant
with them that
I will never
stop
doing good
to them.
I will
fill
their hearts
and minds with respect for me so that they will never again turn away from me.
\VS{41}I will take delight
in doing good
to them. I will faithfully
and wholeheartedly
plant
them firmly in the land.’
\par }{\PP \VS{42}“For
I,
the {\ND{Lord}}, say: ‘I
will surely bring
on
these
people
all
the good
fortune that
I am
hereby promising
them. I will be just
as sure to do
that as I have been in bringing
all
this
great
disaster
on them.
\VS{43}You and your people are saying
that this land
will become desolate,
uninhabited
by either people
or animals.
You are saying that it will
be handed
over to the Babylonians.
But fields
will again be bought
in this
land.
\VS{44}Fields
will again be bought
with silver,
and deeds of purchase
signed,
sealed,
and witnessed.
This
will happen in the territory
of Benjamin,
the villages surrounding
Jerusalem,
the towns
in Judah,
the southern hill country,
the western foothills,
and southern
Judah. For
I will restore
them
to their land. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!’ ”

\par }\Chap{33}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to Jeremiah
a second
time while
he was still
confined
in the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
\VS{2}“I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, do
these things. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, form
the plan to bring
them about. I am known
as the
{\ND{Lord}}. I say to you,
\VS{3}‘Call
on me
in prayer and I will answer
you. I will show
you great
and mysterious
things which you still do not
know about.’
\VS{4}For
I,
the {\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel,
have something more to
say about the houses
in this
city
and the
royal
buildings
which have been torn down
for defenses against the
siege ramps
and military
incursions of the Babylonians:
\VS{5}‘The defenders of the city will go out
and fight
with
the Babylonians.
But they will only fill
those houses and buildings with
the dead bodies
of the people
that
I will kill
in my anger
and my wrath.
That will happen because
I have decided to turn my back on
this
city
on account
of the wicked things they have done.
\VS{6}But I will
most surely
heal the wounds
of this city and restore
it and its people to health.
I will show
them
abundant
peace
and security.
\VS{7}I will restore
Judah
and Israel
and will rebuild
them as they were in days of old.
\VS{8}I will purify
them from all
the sin
that
they committed
against me. I will forgive
all
their sins which
they committed
in rebelling against me.
\VS{9}All
the nations
will hear
about all
the good
things which
I
will do
to them. This city will bring me fame,
honor,
and praise
before them for the joy
that I bring it. The nations will tremble
in awe
at all
the peace
and prosperity
that
I
will provide for it.’
\par }{\PP \VS{10}“I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, say: ‘You
and your people are saying
about this
place, “It lies in ruins.
There are no
people
or
animals
in it.” That
is true. The towns
of Judah
and the streets
of Jerusalem
will soon be desolate,
uninhabited
either by people or by animals.
But happy sounds will again
be heard
in these places.
\VS{11}Once again there will be sounds
of joy
and gladness
and the glad
celebrations
of brides
and grooms.
Once again people will bring
their thank offerings
to the temple
of the
{\ND{Lord}} and will say,
“Give thanks
to the
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
For
the {\ND{Lord}}
is good
and his unfailing
love lasts forever.”
For
I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm that I will restore
the land to what it was in days of old.’
\par }{\PP \VS{12}“I,
the {\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all,
say: ‘This
place
will indeed lie in ruins.
There will be no
people
or animals
in it. But there will again
be in it and in its

sheepfolds

\VS{13}I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, say
that shepherds will once again

the fold. They will do this in all the towns
in the southern hill country,
the western foothills,
the southern
hill country,
the territory of Benjamin,
the villages surrounding
Jerusalem,
and the towns
of Judah.’
\par }{\SH The Lord Reaffirms His Covenant with David, Israel, and Levi

\par }{\SH The Lord Threatens to Destroy Those Who Wronged Their Slaves
\par }{\PP \VS{8}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{9}Everyone

\VS{10}All

\VS{11}But later

\VS{12}That was when

\VS{16}But then you turned right around

\VS{17}So

\VS{18}I will

\VS{19}I will punish the leaders

\VS{20}I will

\VS{21}I will

\VS{22}For I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm

They will fight
against
it and capture

it down.
I will also
make

of Judah
desolate

to

put
Jeremiah
under arrest and took
him to
the officials.
\VS{15}The officials
were very angry
at Jeremiah.
They had
him flogged
and put
in prison
in the house
of Jonathan,
the royal secretary,
which they had converted
into a place for confining prisoners.
\par }{\PP \VS{16}So
Jeremiah
was put
in
prison
in a cell
in the dungeon
in Jonathan’s house. He
was kept
there
for a long
time.
\VS{17}Then
King
Zedekiah
had him brought
to the palace.
There he questioned him
privately
and asked him, “Is there
any message
from the

{\ND{Lord}}?” Jeremiah
answered,
“Yes, there
is.” Then he announced, “You will be handed
over to the king
of Babylon.”
\VS{18}Then Jeremiah
asked
King
Zedekiah,
“What
crime
have I committed against
you, or the officials who serve
you, or the people
of Judah? What have I done to make you people throw
me into
prison?
\VS{19}Where
now are the prophets
who
prophesied
to you that the king
of Babylon
would not
attack
you or this
land?
\VS{20}But now
please
listen,
your royal
Majesty,
and grant
my plea
for mercy.
Do not
send me back
to the house
of Jonathan,
the royal secretary.
If you do,
I will die
there.”
\VS{21}Then
King
Zedekiah
ordered
that Jeremiah
be committed to the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
He also ordered
that a loaf
of bread
be given
to him every day
from
the baker’s
street
until
all
the bread
in the city
was gone.
So Jeremiah
was kept in the courtyard
of the guardhouse.

\par }\Chap{38}{\PP \VerseOne{1}Now
Shephatiah
son
of Mattan,
Gedaliah
son
of Pashhur,
Jehucal
son
of Shelemiah,
and Pashhur
son
of Malkijah
had heard the things
that
Jeremiah
had been telling
the people.
They had heard him say,
\VS{2}“The
{\ND{Lord}}
says,
‘Those who stay
in this
city
will die
in battle
or of starvation
or disease.
Those who leave the city and surrender
to
the Babylonians
will live.
They will
escape
with their lives.’ ”
\VS{3}They had also heard him say, “The
{\ND{Lord}}
says,
‘This
city
will certainly be handed
over to the army
of the king
of Babylon.
They will capture it.’ ”
\VS{4}So these officials
said to
the king,
“This
man

For

in the city
as well

there

This

\VS{5}King
Zedekiah
said
to them,
“Very well, you can
do what you want with
him. For
I cannot
do anything to stop you.”
\VS{6}So the
officials took
Jeremiah
and put him
in
the
cistern
of Malkijah,
one of the royal princes,
that
was in the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
There was no
water
in the cistern, only

So when they lowered
Jeremiah
into the cistern
with ropes
he
sank
in the mud.
\par }{\SH An Ethiopian Official Rescues Jeremiah from the Cistern
\par }{\PP \VS{7}An Ethiopian,
Ebed Melech,
a court official
in the royal
palace,
heard
that
Jeremiah
had been put in the cistern.
While the king
was holding
court at the Benjamin
Gate,
\VS{8}Ebed Melech
departed
the palace
and went to speak
to
the king.
He said to him,
\VS{9}“Your royal
Majesty,
those
men

in all

done

They have

a cistern

there is no

in the city.
\VS{10}Then

gave

the Ethiopian

\VS{11}So

He got

and old

in

\VS{12}Ebed Melech

to

“Put
these rags
and worn-out

under
