to pad
the ropes.
Jeremiah
did
as
Ebed Melech instructed.
\VS{13}So they pulled
Jeremiah
up
from
the cistern
with ropes.
Jeremiah,
however, still remained
confined to the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
\par }{\SH Jeremiah Responds to Zedekiah’s Request for Secret Advice
\par }{\PP \VS{14}Some time later Zedekiah
sent
and had Jeremiah
brought
to
him
at the third

of the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple.
The king
said
to

“I
would like to ask

Do not

anything

\VS{15}Jeremiah
said
to

“If

kill

I give you advice,
you will not
listen
to me.”
\VS{16}So

Zedekiah
made

to

He promised, “As surely
as the
{\ND{Lord}}
lives who has
given

and breath, I promise you this: I will not
kill
you or
hand
you over to those
men
who

to kill you.”
\par }{\PP \VS{17}Then Jeremiah
said
to
Zedekiah,
“The

{\ND{Lord}}, the God
who rules over all,
the God
of Israel,
says, ‘You must
surrender
to

of the king
of Babylon.
If you do, your life

Indeed, you

\VS{18}But if

to

of the king

this

and they will burn

You

\VS{19}Then King

said to

“I am afraid
of the Judeans
who have

The Babylonians might
hand

\VS{20}Then Jeremiah
answered, “You will not
be handed
over to them. Please

the {\ND{Lord}}
by doing what

you. Then all will go well
with you and your life
will be spared.
\VS{21}But if

to surrender,
the {\ND{Lord}}
has shown me a vision of what will happen. Here is
what

\VS{22}All
the women
who
are left
in the royal

of Judah
will be led out
to
the officers
of the king
of Babylon.
They
will taunt you saying,
\par }{\Q ‘Your trusted friends
misled
you;
\par }{\Q they have gotten the best
of you.
\par }{\Q Now that your feet
are stuck
in the mud,
\par }{\Q they have turned
their backs on you.’
\par }{\PP \VS{23}“All

and your children
will be turned
over
to
the Babylonians.
You

by the king
of Babylon.
This
city
will be burned down.”
\par }{\PP \VS{24}Then Zedekiah
told Jeremiah,
“Do
not let anyone
know

\VS{25}The officials

‘Tell

\VS{26}If they do this, tell

‘I

\VS{27}All

He told

\VS{28}So
Jeremiah
remained

until

was captured.
\par }{\SH The Fall of Jerusalem and Its Aftermath
\par }{\PP The following events occurred
when Jerusalem
was captured.

\par }\Chap{39}{\PP \VerseOne{1}King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
came
against Jerusalem
with his whole
army
and laid siege to
it. The siege
began in the tenth
month
of the ninth
year
that Zedekiah
ruled over
Judah.
\VS{2}It lasted until the ninth
day
of the fourth
month
of Zedekiah’s
eleventh
year.
On that day they broke
through the city walls.
\VS{3}Then Nergal-Sharezer
of Samgar, Nebo-Sarsekim,
who was a chief officer,
Nergal-Sharezer,
who was a high official,
and all
the other
officers
of the king
of Babylon
came
and set up quarters
in the Middle
Gate.
\VS{4}When
King
Zedekiah
of Judah
and all
his soldiers
saw them, they tried
to escape.
They departed
from
the city
during the night.
They took a path
through the king’s
garden
and passed out
through the gate
between
the two
walls.
Then
they headed for the Jordan Valley.
\VS{5}But the Babylonian
army
chased
after
them. They caught
up with Zedekiah
in the plains
of Jericho
and captured him. They took
him to
King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
at Riblah
in the territory
of Hamath
and Nebuchadnezzar passed sentence on him there.
\VS{6}There at Riblah
the king
of Babylon
had Zedekiah’s

while Zedekiah was forced to watch.
The king
of Babylon
also had all
the nobles
of Judah
put to death.
\VS{7}Then he had Zedekiah’s
eyes
put out
and had him bound
in chains
to be led off
to Babylon.
\VS{8}The Babylonians
burned down
the
royal
palace,
the temple
of the
{\ND{Lord}}, and the people’s
homes, and they tore
down the wall
of Jerusalem.
\VS{9}Then Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of the royal guard,
took captive
the rest
of the people
who were left
in the city.
He carried
them off to Babylon
along with
the people
who
had deserted to him.
\VS{10}But he left behind
in the land
of Judah
some
of the poor
people
who
owned nothing.
He gave
them fields
and vineyards
at that
time.
\par }{\PP \VS{11}Now King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
had issued orders
concerning
Jeremiah.
He had passed them on through
Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of his royal guard,
\VS{12}“Find
Jeremiah
and look
out for him.
Do not
do
anything
to harm
him, but
do

him whatever
he tells you.”
\VS{13}So Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of the royal guard,
Nebushazban,
who was a chief officer,
Nergal-Sharezer,
who was a high official,
and all
the other officers
of the king
of Babylon
\VS{14}sent

brought
from the courtyard
of the guardhouse.
They turned him over
to
Gedaliah,
the son
of Ahikam
and the grandson of
Shaphan,
to
take
him home
with him. But Jeremiah stayed
among
the people.
\par }{\SH Ebed Melech Is Promised Deliverance because of His Faith
\par }{\PP \VS{15}Now the
{\ND{Lord}}
had
spoken to Jeremiah
while
he was still confined
in the courtyard
of the guardhouse,
\VS{16}“Go
and tell
Ebed-Melech
the Ethiopian,
‘The
{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says,
“I
will carry out
against
this
city

It will mean disaster
and not

for it. When that
disaster happens, you will be there to see it.
\VS{17}But I will
rescue
you
when
it happens. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm

be handed
over to those whom
you

\VS{18}I will certainly
save
you. You will not
fall
victim to violence.
You will escape with your life
because
you trust
in me. I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!” ’ ”

\par }\Chap{40}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to
Jeremiah
after
Nebuzaradan
the captain
of the royal guard
had set him free
at Ramah.
He had taken

along with all

and Judah
who were being carried off
to exile
to Babylon.
\VS{2}The captain
of the royal guard
took

“The
{\ND{Lord}}
your God
threatened

\VS{3}Now he has brought

{\ND{Lord}}
has done

{\ND{Lord}}

\VS{4}But now,

\VS{5}Before

\VS{6}So Jeremiah

to

\par }{\SH A Small Judean Province is Established at Mizpah
\par }{\PP \VS{7}Now some
of the officers
of the Judean army
and their troops had been hiding in the countryside.
They
heard

had appointed
Gedaliah
son

They also heard that

\VS{8}So

\VS{9}Gedaliah,

\VS{10}I

\VS{11}Moreover,

\VS{12}So all

They came
to
Gedaliah
at Mizpah.
Thus they harvested
a large amount
of wine
and dates and figs.
\par }{\SH Ishmael Murders Gedaliah and Carries the Judeans at Mizpah off as Capt
\par }{\PP \VS{13}Johanan
and all
the officers
of the troops
that had
been hiding in the open country

\VS{14}They said

Baalis

\VS{15}Then Johanan

\VS{16}But Gedaliah

\par }\Chap{41}{\PP \VerseOne{1}But in the seventh

\VS{3}Ishmael

\par }{\PP \VS{4}On the day

\VS{6}Ishmael

\VS{10}Then Ishmael

\par }{\SH Johanan Rescues the People Ishmael Had Carried Off
\par }{\PP \VS{11}Johanan

\VS{12}So they took

\VS{13}When

\VS{14}All

\VS{15}But Ishmael

\par }{\PP \VS{16}Johanan

\VS{17}They set out

\VS{18}They were afraid

\par }\Chap{42}{\PP \VerseOne{1}Then all

\VS{2}They said

“Please

For,

\VS{3}Pray that the
{\ND{Lord}}
your God

\VS{4}The prophet
Jeremiah
answered them, “Agreed! I will indeed
pray
to
the {\ND{Lord}}
your God
as

tell you everything
the {\ND{Lord}}

\VS{5}They

“May the
{\ND{Lord}}

the {\ND{Lord}}

\VS{6}We will obey
what
the {\ND{Lord}}
our God
to whom
we
are sending you tells us to
do. It does not matter whether we like what he tells
us
or
not. We
will obey
what
he tells
us to do so
that
things will go well
for us.”
\par }{\PP \VS{7}Ten
days
later
the {\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to Jeremiah.
\VS{8}So Jeremiah summoned
Johanan
son
of Kareah
and all
the army
officers
who
were with
him and all
the people
of every class.
\VS{9}Then Jeremiah said
to them,
“You sent
me to the
{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
to make your request
known to him. Here is what
he says to you:
\VS{10}‘If

stay
in this

I will build
you up. I will not
tear

you. I will not
uproot
you. For

because of the disaster
that

\VS{11}Do not
be afraid
of the king
of Babylon
whom
you

Do not

of him
because

you to save

I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!
\VS{12}I will
have compassion
on you so that he in turn will have mercy
on you and allow you to return
to

\par }{\PP \VS{13}“You
must
not
disobey
the {\ND{Lord}}
your God

‘We will not

in this

\VS{14}You must not say,

and live

\VS{15}If you people who remain
in Judah

The
{\ND{Lord}}

of Israel

to go

\VS{16}the wars

to Egypt.
You will die

\VS{17}All

who

to go
and settle
in Egypt
will die
from war,
starvation,
or disease.
No
one will
survive
or escape
the disaster
I
will bring
on them.’
\VS{18}For
the {\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all

‘If you go to Egypt, I will pour out
my wrath
on

as
I poured out

on
the citizens
of Jerusalem.
You will become
an object of horror
and ridicule,
an example of those who have been cursed
and that people use in pronouncing a curse.
You will never
see
this

again.’
\par }{\PP \VS{19}“The
{\ND{Lord}}
has told
you people who remain
in Judah,
‘Do not
go
to Egypt.’
Be very sure

\VS{20}You are making
a fatal

you
sent

the {\ND{Lord}}
your God
and asked

to
the {\ND{Lord}}
our God

{\ND{Lord}}
our God

\VS{21}This day
I have told you what he said. But you do not
want
to obey
the {\ND{Lord}}
by doing what he sent
me to
tell you.
\VS{22}So now
be very sure
of this: You will die
from war,
starvation,
or disease
in the place
where
you want
to go
and live.”

\par }\Chap{43}{\PP \VerseOne{1}Jeremiah
finished
telling
all

all

things
the {\ND{Lord}}
their God
had
sent

\VS{2}Then Azariah

\VS{3}But

\VS{4}So Johanan

\VS{7}They went

\par }{\SH Jeremiah Predicts that Nebuchadnezzar Will Plunder Egypt and Its Gods
\par }{\PP \VS{8}At Tahpanhes
the {\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to
Jeremiah.
\VS{9}“Take
some large
stones
and bury
them in the mortar
of the clay pavement
at the entrance
of Pharaoh’s
residence
here in Tahpanhes.
Do it while the people of Judah
present there are
watching.
\VS{10}Then tell
them, ‘The

{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says, “I
will bring
my servant
King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon.
I will set
his throne
over
these

which

He will pitch his royal tent
over them.
\VS{11}He will come
and attack
Egypt.
Those who
are destined to die of disease will die of disease. Those who
are destined to be carried off into exile
will
be carried off into exile.
Those who
are destined to
die in war
will die in war.
\VS{12}He will set
fire
to the temples
of the gods
of Egypt.
He will burn
their gods or carry them off as captives.
He will pick Egypt
clean like
a shepherd
picks the lice
from his clothing.
He will leave
there
unharmed.
\VS{13}He will demolish
the sacred pillars
in the temple of the sun
in Egypt
and will burn down
the temples
of the gods
of Egypt.” ’ ”

\par }\Chap{44}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}} spoke
to
Jeremiah
concerning all
the Judeans
who were living
in the land
of Egypt,
those in
Migdol,
Tahpanhes,
Memphis,
and in the region
of southern Egypt.
\VS{2}“The

{\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all
says, ‘You
have seen
all
the disaster
I brought
on
Jerusalem
and all
the towns
of Judah.
Indeed,
they now lie in ruins
and are deserted.
\VS{3}This happened because
of the wickedness
the people living there did.
They made
me angry
by worshiping
and offering sacrifice
to other
gods
whom
neither they
nor you
nor your ancestors
previously knew.
\VS{4}I sent
my servants
the prophets
to you people over and over again
warning

to do
this
disgusting
thing
I hate.
\VS{5}But the people
of Jerusalem and Judah would not listen
or pay
any attention.
They would not stop
the wickedness
they were doing nor quit
sacrificing
to other
gods.
\VS{6}So my anger
and my wrath
were poured
out and burned
like a fire through the towns
of Judah
and the streets
of Jerusalem.
That is why they have become
the desolate
ruins
that they are today.’
\par }{\PP \VS{7}“So now
the

{\ND{Lord}}, the God
who rules over all,
the God
of Israel,
asks, ‘Why
will you
do
such great
harm
to
yourselves? Why should every man,
woman,
child, and baby
of yours be destroyed from the midst
of Judah? Why should you leave yourselves
without a remnant?
\VS{8}That is what will result from your making me angry
by what you are doing.
You are making me angry by sacrificing
to other
gods
here in the land
of Egypt
where
you
live.
You will be destroyed
for doing that! You will become
an example used in curses
and an object of ridicule
among all

\VS{9}Have you forgotten
all the wicked

done
in the towns
of Judah

of Jerusalem

of Judah
and their wives,

\VS{10}To this

contrition! They have not revered
me nor followed
the laws
and statutes
I commanded you
and your ancestors.’
\par }{\PP \VS{11}“Because

the {\ND{Lord}}
God
of Israel
who rules over all

to bring disaster
on you, even to the point of destroying
all

\VS{12}I will see

that

Here in
the land
of Egypt

People of every class
will die
in war
or from starvation.
They will become
an object of horror
and ridicule,
an example of those who have been cursed
and that people use in pronouncing a curse.
\VS{13}I will punish
those who live
in the land
of Egypt
with war,
starvation,
and disease
just

Jerusalem.
\VS{14}None
of the Judean
remnant
who have come
to live
in the land

will
escape
or survive
to return
to the land
of Judah.
Though they
long
to return
and live
there,
none

except

\par }{\PP \VS{15}Then all
the men
who were aware
that
their wives
were sacrificing
to other
gods,
as well as all
their wives,
answered
Jeremiah.
There was a great

all

who lived
in northern
and southern

They answered,
\VS{16}“We will not
listen
to

the {\ND{Lord}}
has

\VS{17}Instead
we will do
everything
we vowed
we would do. We will sacrifice
and pour

to the goddess
called the Queen
of Heaven
just

and our ancestors,
our kings,
and our leaders
previously did
in the towns
of Judah
and in the streets
of Jerusalem.
For then we had plenty
of food,
were well-off,
and had no
troubles.
\VS{18}But ever since
we stopped
sacrificing
and pouring
out drink offerings
to the Queen
of Heaven,
we have been
in great need. Our people have died in wars
or of starvation.”
\VS{19}The women added, “We
did indeed
sacrifice
and pour out
drink offerings
to the Queen
of Heaven.
But
it was with the full knowledge and approval of our husbands
that we made
cakes
in her image
and poured out
drink offerings to her.”
\par }{\PP \VS{20}Then Jeremiah
replied
to
all
the people,
both men
and women,
who responded
to him in this way.
\VS{21}“The

{\ND{Lord}}
did indeed remember
and call to mind

you
and your ancestors,
your kings,
your leaders,
and all the rest of the people
of the land
offered
to other gods in the towns
of Judah
and in the streets
of Jerusalem.
\VS{22}Finally the
{\ND{Lord}}
could
no

endure
your wicked

and the disgusting things
you did.
That
is why your land
has become the desolate,

that it is today.
That
is why it has become a proverbial example used in curses.
\VS{23}You have
sacrificed to other

against the
{\ND{Lord}}! You have not
obeyed
the
{\ND{Lord}}! You have not
followed
his laws,
his statutes,
and his decrees! That is why
this disaster
that is evident
to this

\par }{\PP \VS{24}Then Jeremiah
spoke to
all
the people,
particularly to
all
the women. “Listen
to what
the {\ND{Lord}}
has to say all
you people of Judah
who
are in Egypt.
\VS{25}The

{\ND{Lord}}

who rules over all

‘You

\VS{26}But

{\ND{Lord}}

{\ND{God}} lives….”
\VS{27}I will indeed

not

\VS{28}Some who survive

who have come
to live

\VS{29}Moreover the
{\ND{Lord}}

I
will punish
you in
this

I will do it so that
you will know
that
my threats
to bring

\VS{30}I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, promise
that I will hand
Pharaoh Hophra
king
of Egypt
over
to his enemies
who are seeking
to kill
him. I will do that just
as surely as I handed
King
Zedekiah
of Judah
over
to King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon,
his enemy
who was seeking
to kill him.’ ”

\par }\Chap{45}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The prophet

\par }\Chap{46}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}

\par }{\SH The Prophecy about Egypt’s Defeat at Carchemish
\par }{\PP \VS{2}He spoke about

\par }{\Q \VS{3}“Fall into ranks

\par }{\Q They

\par }{\Q They have been defeated.

\par }{\Q they desert quickly
\par }{\Q without

\par }{\Q Even

\par }{\Q like its streams

\par }{\Q those from Ethiopia

\par }{\Q His sword

{\ND{God}}

\par }{\Q in the land

\par }{\Q you dear poor people

\par }{\Q But it will prove useless

\par }{\Q there will be no

\par }{\Q \VS{12}The nations
will hear

\par }{\Q your cries of distress
will echo throughout
the earth.
\par }{\Q In the panic of their flight one soldier
will trip over
another
\par }{\Q and both

\par }{\SH The Lord Predicts that Nebuchadnezzar Will Attack and Plunder Egypt
\par }{\PP \VS{13}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to

about Nebuchadnezzar

\par }{\Q ‘Take your positions

\par }{\Q \VS{15}Why

\par }{\Q They will not

\par }{\Q I swear as surely as I

\par }{\Q But northern

\par }{\Q when the time

\par }{\Q the time

\par }{\Q as the enemy comes marching up in force.
\par }{\Q They will come

\par }{\Q as if

\par }{\Q \VS{23}The population of Egypt is like a vast, impenetrable

\par }{\Q For

\par }{\Q They

\par }{\Q \VS{24}Poor dear

\par }{\PP \VS{25}The
{\ND{Lord}}

“I

\VS{26}I will hand

and his troops,

I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, affirm it!”
\par }{\SH A Promise of Hope for Israel
\par }{\Q \VS{27}“You
descendants of Jacob,
my servants,
do not
be afraid;
\par }{\Q do not

people of Israel.
\par }{\Q For
I

\par }{\Q from

\par }{\Q The descendants
of Jacob
will return
to their land
and enjoy peace.
\par }{\Q They will be secure

\par }{\Q \VS{28}I, the
{\ND{Lord}}, tell you
not

\par }{\Q you descendants of Jacob,
my servant,
\par }{\Q for
I am
with
you.
\par }{\Q Though
I completely

where
I scatter
you,
\par }{\Q I will not
completely

\par }{\Q I will indeed discipline
you but only in due

\par }{\Q I will not

\par }\Chap{47}{\PP \VerseOne{1}The
{\ND{Lord}}
spoke
to
the prophet
Jeremiah
about the Philistines
before
Pharaoh
attacked
Gaza.
\par }{\Q \VS{2}“Look! Enemies are gathering in the north
like water
rising
in a river.

\par }{\Q They will be
like an overflowing
stream.
\par }{\Q They will overwhelm
the whole country
and everything
in it like a flood.
\par }{\Q They will overwhelm the cities
and their inhabitants.
\par }{\Q People
will cry

\par }{\Q Everyone
living
in the country
will cry out in pain.

\par }{\Q that remains

\par }{\Q when I, the

\par }{\Q No

anger
of the {\ND{Lord}}!
\par }{\Q \VS{46}Do not
lose
your courage
or become
afraid
\par }{\Q because of the reports
that are heard
in the land.
\par }{\Q For a report
will come
in one year.
\par }{\Q Another report
will follow
it in the next.
\par }{\Q There will be violence
in the land
\par }{\Q with ruler
fighting against
ruler.”
\par }{\Q \VS{47}“So
the time
will certainly
come
\par }{\Q when I will punish
the idols
of Babylon.
\par }{\Q Her whole
land
will be put to shame.
\par }{\Q All
her mortally wounded
will collapse
in her midst.
\par }{\Q \VS{48}Then heaven
and earth
and all
that
is in them
\par }{\Q will sing
for joy over
Babylon.
\par }{\Q For
destroyers
from the north
will attack
it,”
\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{49}“Babylon
must fall
\par }{\Q because of the Israelites
she has killed,
\par }{\Q just as
the earth’s
mortally wounded
fell
\par }{\Q because of Babylon.
\par }{\Q \VS{50}You who have escaped
the sword,
\par }{\Q go,
do not
delay.
\par }{\Q Remember
the {\ND{Lord}}
in a faraway
land.
\par }{\Q Think
about Jerusalem.
\par }{\Q \VS{51}‘We are ashamed
because
we
have been insulted.
\par }{\Q Our faces
show our disgrace.
\par }{\Q For
foreigners
have invaded
\par }{\Q the holy rooms
in the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple.’
\par }{\Q \VS{52}Yes,
but the time
will certainly come,”
says
the {\ND{Lord}},

\par }{\Q “when I will punish
her idols.
\par }{\Q Throughout
her land
the mortally wounded
will groan.
\par }{\Q \VS{53}Even if
Babylon
climbs
high into the sky
\par }{\Q and fortifies
her elevated
stronghold,
\par }{\Q I will send
destroyers
against her,”

\par }{\Q says
the {\ND{Lord}}.
\par }{\Q \VS{54}Cries
of anguish
will come from Babylon,
\par }{\Q the sound of great
destruction
from the land
of the Babylonians.
\par }{\Q \VS{55}For
the {\ND{Lord}}
is ready to destroy
Babylon,
\par }{\Q and put an end
to her loud
noise.
\par }{\Q Their waves
will roar
like turbulent
waters.
\par }{\Q They will make
a deafening
noise.
\par }{\Q \VS{56}For
a destroyer
is attacking
Babylon.
\par }{\Q Her warriors
will be captured;
\par }{\Q their bows
will be broken.
\par }{\Q For
the {\ND{Lord}}
is a God
who punishes;
\par }{\Q he pays back in full.
\par }{\Q \VS{57}“I will make her officials
and wise
men drunk,
\par }{\Q along with her governors,
leaders,
and warriors.
\par }{\Q They will fall asleep
forever
and never
wake
up,”

\par }{\Q says
the King
whose name
is the
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all.
\par }{\Q \VS{58}This is what the
{\ND{Lord}}
who rules over all
says,
\par }{\Q “Babylon’s
thick
wall
will be completely demolished.
\par }{\Q Her high
gates
will be set on fire.
\par }{\Q The peoples
strive
for what does not satisfy.
\par }{\Q The nations
grow weary
trying
to get what will be destroyed.”
\par }{\PP \VS{59}This is the order
Jeremiah
the prophet
gave to Seraiah
son
of Neriah,
son
of Mahseiah,
when he went
to
King
Zedekiah
of Judah
in Babylon
during the fourth
year
of his reign.
(Seraiah
was a quartermaster.)
\VS{60}Jeremiah
recorded
on one
scroll
all
the judgments
that
would
come
upon
Babylon
– all
these
prophecies
written
about
Babylon.
\VS{61}Then Jeremiah
said
to
Seraiah,
“When you arrive
in Babylon,
make sure
you read
aloud all
these
prophecies.
\VS{62}Then say,
‘O
{\ND{Lord}}, you
have announced
that you will destroy
this
place
so that no
people
or animals
live
in it any longer. Certainly
it will lie desolate
forever!’
\VS{63}When
you finish
reading
this
scroll
aloud, tie
a stone
to it and throw
it into
the middle
of the Euphrates River.
\VS{64}Then say,
‘In the same
way Babylon
will sink
and never
rise
again because of the judgments
I am
ready to bring
upon
her; they will grow faint.’ ”
\par }{\PP The prophecies
of Jeremiah
end
here.

\par }\Chap{52}{\PP \VerseOne{1}Zedekiah
was twenty-one
years
old when he became king,
and he ruled
in Jerusalem
for eleven
years.
His mother’s
name
was Hamutal
daughter
of Jeremiah,
from Libnah.
\VS{2}He did
what displeased
the {\ND{Lord}}
just
as Jehoiakim
had done.
\par }{\PP \VS{3}What follows is a record of what happened to Jerusalem
and Judah
because
of the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
anger
when he drove
them out of his sight.
Zedekiah
rebelled
against the king
of Babylon.
\VS{4}King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon
came against
Jerusalem
with his whole
army
and set up camp
outside
it. They built
siege ramps
all around
it. He arrived
on the tenth
day of the tenth
month
in the ninth
year
that Zedekiah ruled over Judah.
\VS{5}The city
remained
under siege
until
Zedekiah’s
eleventh
year.
\VS{6}By the ninth
day
of the fourth
month
the famine
in the city
was so severe
the residents
had no
food.
\VS{7}They broke
through the city
walls, and all
the soldiers tried
to escape.
They left
the city
during the night.
They went through
the gate
between
the two walls
that
is near the king’s
garden.
(The Babylonians
had the city
surrounded.) Then
they headed for the Jordan Valley.
\VS{8}But the Babylonian
army
chased
after
the king.
They caught
up with Zedekiah
in the plains
of Jericho,
and his entire
army
deserted
him.
\VS{9}They captured
him and brought him up
to
the king
of Babylon
at Riblah
in the territory
of Hamath
and he passed sentence on him there.
\VS{10}The king
of Babylon
had Zedekiah’s sons
put to death
while Zedekiah
was forced to watch.
He also
had all
the nobles
of Judah
put to death
there at Riblah.
\VS{11}He had Zedekiah’s
eyes
put out
and had him bound
in chains.
Then the king
of Babylon
had him led
off to Babylon
and he was imprisoned
there until
the day
he died.
\par }{\PP \VS{12}On the tenth
day
of the fifth
month,
in the nineteenth
year
of King
Nebuchadnezzar
of Babylon,
Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of the royal guard
who served
the king
of Babylon,
arrived
in Jerusalem.
\VS{13}He burned down
the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple,
the royal
palace,
and all
the houses
in Jerusalem,
including
every
large
house.
\VS{14}The whole
Babylonian
army
that
came with
the captain
of the royal guard
tore
down the walls
that surrounded
Jerusalem.
\VS{15}Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of the royal guard,
took into exile
some
of the poor,
the rest
of the people
who remained
in the city,
those who had deserted
to him, and the
rest
of the craftsmen.
\VS{16}But he left behind
some of the poor
and gave them fields
and vineyards.
\par }{\PP \VS{17}The Babylonians
broke
the
two bronze
pillars
in the temple
of the {\ND{Lord}}, as well as
the
movable stands
and the large bronze
basin called the “The Sea.”
They took
all
the bronze
to Babylon.
\VS{18}They also took
the pots,
shovels,
trimming shears,
basins,
pans,
and all
the bronze
utensils
used by the priests.
\VS{19}The captain
of the royal guard
took
the gold
and silver
bowls,
censers,
basins,
pots,
lampstands,
pans,
and vessels.
\VS{20}The bronze
of the items
that
King
Solomon
made
for the
{\ND{Lord}}’s
temple
(including the two
pillars,
the large bronze basin
called “The Sea,”
the twelve
bronze
bulls
under
“The Sea,” and the movable stands
) was too heavy to be
weighed.
\VS{21}Each of the pillars
was about 27 feet
high,
about 18 feet
in circumference,
three
inches
thick,
and hollow.
\VS{22}The bronze
top of
one
pillar
was about seven and one-half feet
high
and had bronze
latticework
and pomegranate-shaped
ornaments
all
around
it. The second
pillar
with its pomegranate-shaped ornaments was like it.
\VS{23}There were
ninety-six
pomegranate-shaped ornaments
on the sides;
in all
there were one hundred
pomegranate-shaped ornaments
over
the latticework
that went around it.
\par }{\PP \VS{24}The captain
of the royal guard
took
Seraiah
the chief
priest,
Zephaniah
the priest
who was second
in rank, and the three
doorkeepers.
\VS{25}From
the city
he took
an official
who
was in charge of
the soldiers,
seven
of the king’s
advisers
who
were discovered
in the
city,
an official
army
secretary
who drafted
citizens
for military service, and sixty
citizens
who were discovered
in the middle
of the city.
\VS{26}Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of the royal guard,
took
them and brought
them to
the king
of Babylon
at Riblah.
\VS{27}The king
of Babylon
ordered
them to be executed
at Riblah
in the territory
of Hamath.
\par }{\PP So Judah
was taken into exile
away from its land.
\VS{28}Here
is the official record of the number of people
Nebuchadnezzar
carried into exile: In the seventh
year,
3,023
Jews;
\VS{29}in Nebuchadnezzar’s
eighteenth
year,
832
people
from Jerusalem;
\VS{30}in Nebuchadnezzar’s
twenty-third
year,
Nebuzaradan,
the captain
of the royal guard,
carried into exile
745
Judeans.
In all
4,600
people went into exile.
\par }{\SH Jehoiachin in Exile
\par }{\PP \VS{31}In the thirty-seventh
year
of the exile
of King
Jehoiachin
of Judah,
on the twenty-fifth
day of the twelfth
month,
Evil-Merodach,
in the first year
of his reign,
pardoned
King
Jehoiachin
of Judah
and released
him from prison.
\VS{32}He spoke
kindly
to him
and gave
him a more prestigious
position
than the other kings
who
were with
him in Babylon.
\VS{33}Jehoiachin took off
his prison
clothes
and ate
daily
in the king’s presence
for the rest
of his life.
\VS{34}He was given
daily
provisions
by the king
of Babylon
for the rest of his life until
the day
he died.

\par }
